Names and Rulings: Theological Labels and Their Consequences
Sanusi defines the terms 'names' and 'rulings' as used by early scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of 'names' and 'rulings' as used by early Sunni theologians and how these terms set the stage for discussions on the definition of faith.

Core Idea
In theology, 'names' are labels of praise or blame, and 'rulings' are their eternal consequences.

Sanusi begins the third chapter by clarifying the terminology that will govern the ensuing discussion. Before diving into the definition of faith and other doctrinal questions, we must first agree on what the key terms mean. This passage establishes that 'names' refer to the commendatory or disparaging labels applied to morally responsible persons, and 'rulings' refer to the reward or punishment attached to each label.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Notice the concise definition style.
Pay attention to the examples of praise and blame.
2
Identify the two categories
Find how Sanusi defines 'names' (الأسماء) and 'rulings' (الأحكام). Note the examples of praise (مدح) and blame (ذم).
The examples help solidify the meaning.
3
Connect to the broader context
Understand that this chapter is foundational for later discussions about faith and the status of believers and sinners.
This terminology appears in many classical works.
4
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to test your comprehension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : الفصل الثالث في الأسماء والأحكام: وفيه مباحث . هذه الترجمة شائعة في كلام المتقدمين، ويعنون بالأسماء أسامي المكلفين في المدح، مثل المؤمن والمسلم، والمتقي، والصالح، وفي الذم مثل الكافر والفاسق والمنافق . وبالأحكام ما لكل منها في الآخرة من الثواب والعقاب وكيفيتهما .
He said: The third chapter concerning names (al-asmā') and rulings (al-aḥkām). It contains investigations. This title is common in the speech of the earlier scholars. By 'names' they mean the names of the legally responsible persons in praise, such as believer, Muslim, God-fearing, and righteous; and in blame, such as disbeliever, sinner, and hypocrite. By 'rulings' they mean what each of them will have in the afterlife of reward, punishment, and their modalities.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is an introductory summary for the chapter on al-asmā' wa al-aḥkām (names and rulings). The author explains that this terminology was common among the early scholars. 'Names' refers to the labels applied to morally responsible individuals (mukallafūn)—either commendatory (e.g., believer, Muslim) or disparaging (e.g., disbeliever, sinner, hypocrite). 'Rulings' refers to the eschatological consequences—reward or punishment, and the manner thereof—that correspond to each name. This sets the stage for the detailed discussion that follows on the definition of īmān (faith).

Linguistic Definition of Iman and Its Etymological Derivation
Sanusi defines iman linguistically as tasdiq, derives it from amn, and discusses its prepositional usage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic definition of iman (faith) as tasdiq (affirmation), its derivation from the root amn, and how its usage with the prepositions bi and lam conveys nuances of acknowledgment and submission.

Core Idea
Iman linguistically means affirmation (tasdiq), rooted in security (amn) and expressed through acknowledgment and submission.

Sanusi begins by establishing the linguistic foundation of iman, which is essential for theological discussions. The word iman is traced back to its root meaning of security and is defined as tasdiq (affirmation). He then explains how the verb is used with different prepositions to capture specific connotations of acknowledgment and submission, supported by Qur'anic examples. This lesson unpacks these linguistic details to clarify the precise meaning of faith in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overview of the content.
Pay attention to the technical terms.
2
Identify the linguistic definition and derivation
Note that iman is defined as tasdiq (affirmation) and is derived from amn (security) as a verbal noun (if‘āl).
Derivation shows a semantic connection to security.
3
Understand the prepositions
Observe how iman is used with bi (acknowledgment) and lam (submission) and the examples given.
The prepositions reflect different nuances.
4
Reflect on the etymological insight
Consider the idea that the one who affirms becomes secure from being belied, or makes others secure from denial.
This ties the linguistic meaning back to its root.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الأول - الإيمان في اللغة التصديق، إفعال من الأمن للصيرورة أو التعدية . ويعدى بالباء واللام لملاحظة معنى الاعتراف والإذعان، ولما أن مآله إلى أخذ الشيء صادقاً، والصدق مما يوصف به المتكلم، والكلام والحكم تعلق بالشيء باعتبارات مختلفة مثل : آمنت بالله وبالملائكة، وبالكتاب، وبالرسول، وباليوم الآخر، وبالقدر . بحسب الأصل كأن المصدق صار ذا أمن من أن يكون مكذوباً ، أو جعل الغير آمناً من التكذيب والمخالفة. ويعدى بالباء لاعتبار معنى الإقرار والاعتراف كقوله تعالى: آمن الرسول بما أنزل لليه) (٣) وباللام لاعتبار معنى الإذعان والقبول كقوله تعالى حكاية وما أنت بمؤمن
He said: The first investigation — faith (al-īmān) in language is affirmation (al-taṣdīq), a verbal noun from amn (security) for becoming or transitive sense. It is made transitive with bi (by) and lām (for) to observe the meaning of acknowledgment and submission, and because its final outcome is taking something as true. Truthfulness (al-ṣidq) is attributed to the speaker, speech, and judgment; it relates to the thing by various considerations, such as: I believe in God, in the angels, in the Book, in the Messenger, in the Last Day, and in predestination. Essentially, it is as if the one who affirms has become secure from being belied (made false), or has made others secure from denial and opposition. It is made transitive with bi (by) to consider the meaning of acknowledgment and confession, like His statement: 'The Messenger believes in what has been sent down to him' (Qur'an 2:285), and with lām (for) to consider the meaning of submission and acceptance, like His statement, narrated: 'And you are not a believer for us' (Qur'an 12:17).
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage defines īmān (faith) linguistically and explains its derivation. It begins by stating that īmān in language means taṣdīq (affirmation, believing). It is derived from the root amn (security) and formed as if‘āl, indicating either becoming or making transitive. The verb is made transitive with the prepositions bi and lām to capture nuances of acknowledgment (i‘tirāf) and submission (idh‘ān), because the ultimate meaning is accepting something as true. The author notes that truthfulness can be attributed to the speaker, speech, or judgment, and provides examples with the preposition bi, such as believing in God, angels, etc. The passage then adds an etymological explanation: the one who affirms (muṣaddiq) becomes secure from being refuted, or makes others secure from denial. It concludes by distinguishing the uses of bi (emphasizing acknowledgment) and lām (emphasizing submission), citing Qur'anic verses.

Key Terms

تصديق
أمن
إفعال
اعتراف
إذعان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iman simply means belief in a generic sense without linguistic depth.
Correction: The linguistic root of iman is security (amn), and it specifically means affirmation (tasdiq) with connotations of acknowledgment and submission, as shown by its prepositional usage.

Checkpoint

A) Knowledge (ma'rifa).
B) Affirmation (tasdiq).
C) Action (amal).
D) Submission (islam).

Key Takeaway
Iman linguistically means affirmation (tasdiq) and is derived from security (amn), used with prepositions to emphasize acknowledgment and submission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says that the one who affirms (muṣaddiq) becomes secure from being belied. In your own life, when you affirm your faith in Allah—truly and deeply—does it bring you a sense of security and peace? If not, what might be lacking in your affirmation? Commit today to affirm one article of faith with full certainty, and observe how it affects your inner state.
?
Iman with the preposition bi emphasizes acknowledgment and confession. You recite the shahada regularly, but does your heart truly acknowledge each word? Are there areas of your life where your confession contradicts your actions? Resolve to align your deeds with your confession, starting with one specific behavior you will change this week.
?
The lesson teaches that iman also involves submission (idh‘ān) as shown by the preposition lām. Is there an area of your life where you have not yet submitted to Allah's command—perhaps a habit, a relationship, or a fear? What would it look like for you to truly submit in that area? The Four Sharia Definitions of Faith (Iman)
Sanusi enumerates the four Sharia definitions of iman with detailed sub-opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four main Sharia definitions of faith (iman) and the key differences among the schools regarding the role of action.

Core Idea
Faith in Sharia is defined by heart, tongue, both, or all three plus action.

In this passage, Sanusi lays out the four major Sharia definitions of iman, each with its proponents and variants. This is a crucial classification for understanding debates on the nature of faith across Islamic theological schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
Read the passage and locate the four main categories: heart only, tongue only, both, or both plus limbs. Notice the Arabic phrasing.
The categories are introduced with 'إما أن يجعل لفعل القلب فقط، أو اللسان فقط، أو كليهما وحدهما أو مع سائر الجوارح'.
2
Examine subdivisions within each
For each category, note the different groups and conditions mentioned. For example, under 'heart only' there are two views: taṣdīq (majority) and ma‘rifa (Shia, etc.).
Pay attention to the names: al-Raqqāshī, al-Qaṭṭān, Karāmiyya, etc.
3
Understand the fourth category’s three positions
The fourth category (faith includes actions) has three sub-views: Khawārij (abandoner of action is kāfir), Mu‘tazila (abandoner not kāfir but not in faith), and Salaf (abandoner not outside faith, distinguishing core and perfect faith).
Note the logical conclusion about part and whole at the end.
4
Reflect on the logical principle
Consider the final sentence: 'the non-existence of a thing by the non-existence of its part is necessary.' How does this relate to the Salaf view?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في الشرع فإما أن يجعل لفعل القلب فقط، أو اللسان فقط، أو كليهما وحدهما أو مع سائر الجوارح. فعلى الأول هو اسم للتصديق عند الأكثرين، أعني تصديق النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) فيما علم مجيئه به بالضرورة. وللمعرفة عند الشيعة، وجهم، والصالحي. وعلى الثاني للإقرار بشرط المعرفة عند الرقاشي، وبشرط التصديق عند القطان ، وبلا شرط عند الكرامية . وعلى الثالث لمجموع التصديق والإقرار وعليه أكثر المحققين، إلا أنه كثيراً ما يقع في عباراتهم مكان التصديق المعرفة أو العلم أو الاعتقاد . وعلى الرابع للإقرار باللسان، والتصديق بالجنان، والعمل بالأركان ، إما على أن يجعل تارك العمل خارجاً عن الإيمان، داخلاً في الكفر، وعليه الخوارج، أو غير داخل فيه، وعليه المعتزلة، مختلفين في أن الأعمال فعل الواجبات، وترك المحظورات، أو مطلق فعل الطاعات وإما على أن لا يجعل خارجاً وعليه أكثر السلف. وهو المحكي عن مالك والشافعي ذهاباً إلى أنه قد يطلق على ما هو الأساس في النجاة. وعلى الكامل المنجي بلا خلاف وإلا فانتفاء الشيء بانتفاء جزئه (ضروري)
As for in Sharia, it is either made to be an act of the heart only, or of the tongue only, or both alone, or along with the other limbs. According to the first, it (faith) is a name for affirmation (taṣdīq) according to the majority, meaning affirmation of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in what is known necessarily to have come from him; and for knowledge (ma‘rifa) according to the Shī‘a, Jahm, and al-Ṣāliḥī. According to the second, it is for confession (iqrār) with the condition of knowledge according to al-Raqqāshī, with the condition of affirmation according to al-Qaṭṭān, and without condition according to the Karāmiyya. According to the third, it is for the combination of affirmation and confession, and this is the view of most of the verifiers, except that often in their expressions, in place of affirmation, they use knowledge, science, or belief. According to the fourth, it is for confession by the tongue, affirmation by the heart, and action by the limbs; either making the abandoner of action outside faith, inside unbelief — and this is the view of the Khawārij; or not inside it (faith) — and this is the view of the Mu‘tazila, differing as to whether actions are the performance of obligations and abandonment of prohibitions, or absolute performance of acts of obedience; or making him not outside faith — and this is the view of most of the Salaf. This is related from Mālik and al-Shāfi‘ī, holding that it (faith) may be applied to that which is the basis of salvation, and to the perfect saving faith without dispute; otherwise, the non-existence of a thing by the non-existence of its part is necessary.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage classifies the Sharia definitions of īmān (faith) into four main categories. The first defines faith as an act of the heart only: either taṣdīq (affirmation) according to the majority (Ahl al-Sunna), or ma‘rifa (knowledge) according to the Shī‘a, Jahm, and al-Ṣāliḥī. The second defines faith as an act of the tongue only (iqrār, confession), with sub-views on whether knowledge or affirmation is required. The third defines faith as both heart affirmation and tongue confession, which is the view of most investigating scholars, though they sometimes use 'knowledge' or 'belief' interchangeably. The fourth adds actions of the limbs to heart affirmation and tongue confession, with three sub-views: the Khawārij consider action a necessary part such that its absence removes one from faith entirely (kufr); the Mu‘tazila consider action a necessary part but do not place the abandoner in kufr, though they disagree on what actions count; and the majority of the Salaf (including Mālik and al-Shāfi‘ī) do not consider the abandoner of action as outside faith, but rather distinguish between the core of faith (the basis of salvation) and its perfect form. The passage ends with a logical note: the non-existence of the whole necessarily follows from the non-existence of an essential part.

Key Terms
إيمان
شرع
تصديق
إقرار
عمل
معرفة
خوارج
معتزلة
سلف
كرامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The fourth definition (faith includes actions) necessarily means that abandoning actions removes one from the category of faith entirely.
Correction: Only the Khawārij hold that view; the Mu‘tazila hold a middle position, and the majority of the Salaf (including Mālik and al-Shāfi‘ī) do not remove the abandoner from faith but distinguish between the core basis of salvation and the perfect form.

Checkpoint
According to the majority of the Salaf (including Malik and al-Shafi'i), what is the status of one who abandons actions?
A) He becomes a disbeliever (kafir).
B) He is outside faith but not in kufr.
C) He is not outside faith; faith may be applied to the basis of salvation.
D) He is considered a hypocrite.

Key Takeaway
The Sharia definition of faith is not monolithic; it ranges from mere heart affirmation to a composite of heart, tongue, and limbs, with each view having its own theological implications.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the four definitions resonates most with your actual experience of iman? Is your faith confined to heart and tongue, or does it compel your limbs to act? What does your answer reveal about your understanding of salvation?
?
The Salaf held that abandoning actions does not remove you from the basis of faith, yet they did not use this as a license to sin. Are you, in your own life, using this theological position as an excuse for negligence, or does it spur you to seek the perfect faith that includes action?
?
If you truly believed that iman could be reduced to mere affirmation or confession, would your daily priorities shift? Pause and consider: what would you lose or gain if actions were not part of the definition of faith?

Tasdiq: Voluntary Affirmation as the Core of Faith
Sanusi defines tasdiq as volitional assent and contrasts it with denial, hesitation, and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tasdiq (affirmation) is a voluntary act of the heart distinct from mere knowledge, and that it is the essence of iman.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is not just knowing; it is choosing to affirm.

The author begins by defining tasdiq in contrast to its opposites—takdhib (denial) and taraddud (hesitation). He immediately notes that tasdiq is not the same as 'ilm or ma'rifa (knowledge), because disbelievers can know the truth without affirming it. This distinction is crucial for understanding the nature of faith as a volitional commitment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify key terms
Read the Arabic passage once, noting the terms tasdiq, takdhib, taraddud, 'ilm, and ma'rifa. Then read the translation.
Pay attention to how the author uses opposites to define tasdiq.
2
Understand the distinction between tasdiq and ma'rifa
The author states that tasdiq is not the same as knowledge, citing Quranic verses showing that disbelievers knew but did not affirm. Notice the difference in their opposites.
3
Grasp the voluntary nature of tasdiq
Tasdiq is described as kashbi ikhtiyari (acquired and voluntary), commanded and rewarded. Contrast this with ma'rifa which may be involuntary.
This distinguishes tasdiq from the logical term used in philosophy.
4
Reflect on the implication for faith
The criterion for iman is voluntary tasdiq. Ask yourself why choice is essential for faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقابله التكذيب وينافيه التردد، وهو غير العلم والمعرفة، لأن من الكفار من كان يعرف ولا يصدق. قال الله: الذين آتيناهم الكتاب يعرفونه كما يعرفون أبناءهم) (۱) وإن الذين أوتوا الكتاب ليعلمون أنه الحق (۲) وجحدوا بها واستيقنتها أنفسهم (۳). وبين الفرق بأن المقابل للتصديق الإنكار والتكذيب، وللمعرفة النكر والجهالة. ولهذا قد يفسر بالتسليم وبالعكس وبأن التصديق ربط القلب على ما علم من إخبار المخبر، وهو كسبي اختياري، ولهذا يؤمر به ويثاب عليه. والمعرفة ربما تحصل بلا كسب. ولقد زاد من قال المعتبر في الإيمان التصديق الاختياري. ومعناه نسبة الصدق إلى المتكلم اختياراً. وبهذا يمتاز عما جعل في المنطق مقابلاً للتصور فإنه قد يخلو عن الاختيار فلا يكون تصديقاً في اللغة، فلا يكون إيماناً في الشرع، كيف والتصديق مأمور به، فيكون فعلاً اختيارياً هو إيقاع النسبة اختياراً، والعلم كيفية نفسانية أو انفعال). في اللغة التصديق بشهادة النقل عن أئمة اللغة ودلالة موارد الاستعمال. ولم ينقل في الشرع إلى معنى آخر. أما أولاً، فلأن النقل خلاف الأصل لا يصار إليه إلا بدليل. وأما ثانياً، فلأنه كثر في الكتاب والسنة خطاب العرب به. بل كان ذلك أول الواجبات وأساس المشروعات، فامتثل من امتثل من غير استفسار ولا توقف إلى بيان ولم يكن ذلك من الخطاب بما لا يفهم وإنما احتيج إلى بيان ما يجب الإيمان به فبين وفصل بعض التفصيل، حيث قال النبي (عليه السلام) لمن سأله عن الإيمان: الإيمان أن تؤمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله... الحديث. فذكر لفظ تؤمن بالله تعويلاً على ظهور معناه عندهم. ثم قال: هذا جبرائيل أتاكم يعلمكم دينكم. ولو كان الإيمان غير التصديق، لما كان هذا تعليماً وإرشاداً، بل تلبساً وإضلالاً. نعم لو قيل إنه في اللغة لمطلق التصديق، وقد نقل في الشرع إلى التصديق بأمور مخصوصة، فلا نزاع. وإنما المقصود أنه تصديق بالأمور المخصوصة بالمعنى اللغوي، وهو ما يعبر عنه بالفارسية بكرويدن وراستكوي داشتن ويخالفه التكذيب، وينافيه التوقف والتردد. ولهذا اختار العلماء في ألفاظ الإيمان كرويدم باور داشتم راستكوي داشتم، بدل، وأنه معنى واضح عند العقل لا يشتبه على العوام، فضلاً عن الخواص والمذهب أنه غير العلم والمعرفة، لأن من الكفار من كان يعرف الحق ولا يصدق به عناداً واستكباراً. قال الله تعالى: الذين آتيناهم الكتاب يعرفونه كما يعرفون أبناءهم وإن فريقاً منهم ليكتمون الحق وهم يعلمون) (۱). وقال: وإن الذين أوتوا الكتاب ليعلمون أنه الحق من ربهم وما الله بغافل عما يعملون) (٢). وقال: وجحدوا بها واستيقنتها أنفسهم ظلماً وعلوا (۳) وقال حكاية عن موسى (عليه السلام) لفرعون ولقد علمت ما أنزل هؤلاء إلا رب السموات والأرض بصائر) (٤) فاحتيج إلى الفرق بين العلم بما جاء به النبي (عليه السلام) وهو معرفته، وبين التصديق ليصح كون الأول حاصلاً للمعاندين، دون الثاني، وكون الثاني إيماناً دون الأول. فاقتصر بعضهم على أن ضد التصديق هو الإنكار والتكذيب، وضد المعرفة النكارة والجهالة. وإليه أشار الإمام الغزالي (رحمه الله) حيث فسر التصديق بالتسليم فإنه لا يكون مع الإنكار والاستكبار، بخلاف العلم
And its opposite is takdhib (denial) and its contradictory is taraddud (hesitation), and it [tasdiq] is other than 'ilm (knowledge) and ma'rifa (cognition), because among the disbelievers were those who knew (ya'rifu) but did not affirm (yusaddiq). Allah said: 'Those to whom We gave the Book recognize it as they recognize their sons' (1) and 'Indeed those who were given the Book know that it is the truth' (2) and 'They denied them, though their souls were convinced of them' (3). And the difference [between tasdiq and ma'rifa] is explained: the opposite of tasdiq is inkar (rejection) and takdhib; the opposite of ma'rifa is nakara (ignorance) and jahala (ignorance). For this reason, it [tasdiq] may be interpreted as taslim (submission) and vice versa, and that tasdiq is the binding of the heart to what one knows from the informant's report, and it is acquired and voluntary (kashbi ikhtiyari), and therefore one is commanded to do it and rewarded for it. But ma'rifa may be obtained without acquisition. And indeed he who said that the criterion in iman (faith) is ikhtiyari tasdiq (voluntary affirmation) has added [something]. Its meaning is ascribing truthfulness to the speaker voluntarily. By this it is distinguished from what is made in logic as the counterpart of tasawwur (conception), for it may be devoid of choice, so it would not be tasdiq in language, so it would not be iman in the Shari'a. How [could it be]? And tasdiq is commanded, so it is a voluntary act, which is effecting the relation voluntarily, while 'ilm is a psychical quality or passion. In language, tasdiq [is proven] by the testimony of transmission from the imams of language and the indication of contexts of usage. And it was not transferred in the Shari'a to another meaning. As for first, because transfer is contrary to the principle, and recourse is not made to it except with evidence. As for second, because in the Book and the Sunnah the address to the Arabs with it is frequent. Rather it was the first of obligations and the foundation of legislated matters, so those who complied did so without inquiry or hesitation for explanation, and that was not an address with what is not understood, but rather there was need to explain what must be believed in, so he explained and detailed some detail, when the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the one who asked him about iman: 'Iman is that you believe (tu'min) in Allah, His angels, His books, and His messengers...' the hadith. So he mentioned the word tu'min (you believe) relying on the clearness of its meaning among them. Then he said: 'This is Jibril, he came to teach you your religion.' And if iman were other than tasdiq, this would not be teaching and guidance, but rather confusion and misguidance. Yes, if it is said that it [iman] in language is absolute tasdiq, and in the Shari'a it was transferred to tasdiq of specific matters, then there is no dispute. Rather the intended meaning is that it is tasdiq of the specific matters in the linguistic sense, which is expressed in Persian as 'karvidan' and 'rasti dashtan', and it is opposed by takdhib, and its contradictory is tawquf (stopping) and taraddud. And therefore scholars chose in the expressions of iman: 'karvidam', 'bawur dashtam', 'rasti dashtam', instead, and that it is a meaning clear in the intellect, not confused for the common people, let alone the elite. And the doctrine is that it [iman] is other than 'ilm and ma'rifa, because among the disbelievers were those who knew the truth but did not affirm it out of obstinacy and arrogance. Allah Almighty said: 'Those to whom We gave the Book recognize it as they recognize their sons, and indeed a party of them conceal the truth while they know' (1). And He said: 'And indeed those who were given the Book know that it is the truth from their Lord, and Allah is not unaware of what they do' (2). And He said: 'And they denied them [the signs], though their souls were convinced of them, out of injustice and haughtiness' (3). And He related from Moses (peace be upon him) to Pharaoh: 'And you certainly know that none has sent down these [signs] except the Lord of the heavens and the earth as insights' (4). So there was need to distinguish between knowledge of what the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought—which is ma'rifa of it—and tasdiq, so that it is correct that the former is possessed by the obstinate, but not the latter, and that the latter is iman and not the former. So some confined themselves [to saying] that the opposite of tasdiq is inkar and takdhib, and the opposite of ma'rifa is nakara and jahala. And Imam al-Ghazali (may Allah have mercy on him) alluded to this where he interpreted tasdiq as taslim, for it does not accompany inkar and istikbar (arrogance), unlike 'ilm.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage defines tasdiq (affirmation/assent) as the core of iman (faith) and distinguishes it sharply from 'ilm or ma'rifa (knowledge/cognition). The author begins by stating that tasdiq is opposed by takdhib (denial) and contradictory to taraddud (hesitation). It is not the same as knowledge, because many disbelievers had knowledge of the truth—as shown by Quranic verses—yet did not affirm it. The key difference is that the opposite of tasdiq is inkar (rejection) and takdhib, while the opposite of ma'rifa is nakara (ignorance) and jahala. Tasdiq is an acquired, voluntary act (kashbi ikhtiyari); it is binding the heart to what one knows from the informant, and it is commanded and rewarded. In contrast, ma'rifa may occur without any voluntary acquisition. The author then emphasizes that the criterion in iman is voluntary tasdiq (ikhtari tasdiq), meaning ascribing truthfulness to the speaker by choice. This distinguishes it from the logical term 'tasdiq' which is the counterpart of tasawwur (conception) and may be involuntary; such involuntary assent would not be tasdiq in the linguistic sense, and thus not iman in the Shari'a. The author then provides proof from language and revelation that the term 'iman' in the Shari'a retains its linguistic meaning of tasdiq, not transferred to a new meaning. He argues that transfer is contrary to the default principle and requires evidence, and that the Quran and Sunnah frequently address the Arabs with this word without needing explanation—indeed, the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Jibril defined iman as 'to believe in Allah...' relying on the clear meaning of 'tu'min' (you believe). If iman were not tasdiq, this teaching would be confusing rather than instructive. The author then notes that if someone claims that iman in language is absolute tasdiq but in Shari'a it is tasdiq of specific matters, then there is no real dispute; the intended meaning is that iman is tasdiq of those specific matters in the linguistic sense, expressed in Persian as 'karvidan' and 'rasti dashtan'. He reiterates the doctrine that iman is distinct from mere knowledge, citing Quranic verses showing that disbelievers had knowledge but not affirmation due to obstinacy. Thus a distinction is necessary: ma'rifa can coexist with obstinacy, but tasdiq cannot. Some scholars have therefore defined tasdiq as taslim (submission), which excludes rejection and arrogance, unlike mere knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That knowledge (ma'rifa) alone constitutes faith.
Correction: The author shows that faith requires volitional assent (tasdiq), which is distinct from involuntary knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is the opposite of tasdiq according to the passage?
A) Ma'rifa
B) Takdhib
C) Taraddud
D) 'Ilm

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq is a voluntary act of affirmation distinct from mere knowledge, and it is the essence of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have known the truth of Islam for years—but have you genuinely bound your heart to it by choice? When did you last consciously affirm a core belief as an act of your own will, not just as inherited knowledge?
?
Is there any area of your life where you 'recognize the truth as you recognize your own children,' yet your heart hesitates or holds back? What would it cost you to replace that hesitation with full tasdiq?
?
If tasdiq is voluntary and you are commanded to do it, what is your heart's posture right now—are you actively choosing to affirm, or merely coasting on intellectual assent? Name one belief you will affirm deliberately today.

What Is Kalam?
beginner
5 min
The Linguistic and Shari'a Continuity of Iman as Tasdiq
Sanusi argues that 'iman' in Shari'a retains its linguistic meaning of tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the term 'iman' in the Shari'a retains its original linguistic meaning of tasdiq (affirmation), and that the Prophet's teaching confirms this understanding.

Core Idea
Iman is tasdiq in both language and revelation; no transfer occurred.

The author now addresses a potential objection: has the term 'iman' been transferred in the Shari'a to a new meaning? He argues that no such transfer took place, because the default is no transfer, and the usage in Quran and Sunnah confirms the linguistic sense. The Prophet himself used the word 'tu'min' in defining iman, relying on its clear meaning among the Arabs.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of no transfer
The author states that transfer from original meaning is contrary to the principle and requires evidence. Read this part carefully.
This is a key rule in usul.
2
Observe the frequency of usage
The Quran and Sunnah address the Arabs with the word 'iman' frequently, showing they understood it in its common sense.
3
Analyze the hadith of Jibril
The Prophet defined iman using 'tu'min', which is derived from iman/tasdiq. This shows the linguistic meaning is the Shari'a meaning.
If iman were different, the Prophet's answer would be confusing.
4
Consider the implication
If iman were not tasdiq, the Prophet's teaching would not be guidance but confusion. This solidifies the continuity.

وجحدوا بها واستيقنتها أنفسهم (۳). وبين الفرق بأن المقابل للتصديق الإنكار والتكذيب، وللمعرفة النكر والجهالة. ولهذا قد يفسر بالتسليم وبالعكس وبأن التصديق ربط القلب على ما علم من إخبار المخبر، وهو كسبي اختياري، ولهذا يؤمر به ويثاب عليه. والمعرفة ربما تحصل بلا كسب. ولقد زاد من قال المعتبر في الإيمان التصديق الاختياري. ومعناه نسبة الصدق إلى المتكلم اختياراً. وبهذا يمتاز عما جعل في المنطق مقابلاً للتصور فإنه قد يخلو عن الاختيار فلا يكون تصديقاً في اللغة، فلا يكون إيماناً في الشرع، كيف والتصديق مأمور به، فيكون فعلاً اختيارياً هو إيقاع النسبة اختياراً، والعلم كيفية نفسانية أو انفعال). في اللغة التصديق بشهادة النقل عن أئمة اللغة ودلالة موارد الاستعمال. ولم ينقل في الشرع إلى معنى آخر. أما أولاً، فلأن النقل خلاف الأصل لا يصار إليه إلا بدليل. وأما ثانياً، فلأنه كثر في الكتاب والسنة خطاب العرب به. بل كان ذلك أول الواجبات وأساس المشروعات، فامتثل من امتثل من غير استفسار ولا توقف إلى بيان ولم يكن ذلك من الخطاب بما لا يفهم وإنما احتيج إلى بيان ما يجب الإيمان به فبين وفصل بعض التفصيل، حيث قال النبي (عليه السلام) لمن سأله عن الإيمان: الإيمان أن تؤمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله... الحديث. فذكر لفظ تؤمن بالله تعويلاً على ظهور معناه عندهم. ثم قال: هذا جبرائيل أتاكم يعلمكم دينكم. ولو كان الإيمان غير التصديق، لما كان هذا تعليماً وإرشاداً، بل تلبساً وإضلالاً. نعم لو قيل إنه في اللغة لمطلق التصديق، وقد نقل في الشرع إلى التصديق بأمور مخصوصة، فلا نزاع. وإنما المقصود أنه تصديق بالأمور المخصوصة بالمعنى اللغوي، وهو ما يعبر عنه بالفارسية بكرويدن وراستكوي داشتن ويخالفه التكذيب، وينافيه التوقف والتردد. ولهذا اختار العلماء في ألفاظ الإيمان كرويدم باور داشتم راستكوي داشتم، بدل، وأنه معنى واضح عند Commentary
This passage defines tasdiq (affirmation/assent) as the core of iman (faith) and distinguishes it sharply from 'ilm or ma'rifa (knowledge/cognition). The author begins by stating that tasdiq is opposed by takdhib (denial) and contradictory to taraddud (hesitation). It is not the same as knowledge, because many disbelievers had knowledge of the truth—as shown by Quranic verses—yet did not affirm it. The key difference is that the opposite of tasdiq is inkar (rejection) and takdhib, while the opposite of ma'rifa is nakara (ignorance) and jahala. Tasdiq is an acquired, voluntary act (kashbi ikhtiyari); it is binding the heart to what one knows from the informant, and it is commanded and rewarded. In contrast, ma'rifa may occur without any voluntary acquisition. The author then emphasizes that the criterion in iman is voluntary tasdiq (ikhtari tasdiq), meaning ascribing truthfulness to the speaker by choice. This distinguishes it from the logical term 'tasdiq' which is the counterpart of tasawwur (conception) and may be involuntary; such involuntary assent would not be tasdiq in the linguistic sense, and thus not iman in the Shari'a. The author then provides proof from language and revelation that the term 'iman' in the Shari'a retains its linguistic meaning of tasdiq, not transferred to a new meaning. He argues that transfer is contrary to the default principle and requires evidence, and that the Quran and Sunnah frequently address the Arabs with this word without needing explanation—indeed, the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Jibril defined iman as 'to believe in Allah...' relying on the clear meaning of 'tu'min' (you believe). The author then notes that if someone claims that iman in language is absolute tasdiq but in Shari'a it is tasdiq of specific matters, then there is no real dispute; the intended meaning is that iman is tasdiq of those specific matters in the linguistic sense, expressed in Persian as 'karvidan' and 'rasti dashtan'. He reiterates the doctrine that iman is distinct from mere knowledge, citing Quranic verses showing that disbelievers had knowledge but not affirmation due to obstinacy. Thus a distinction is necessary: ma'rifa can coexist with obstinacy, but tasdiq cannot. Some scholars have therefore defined tasdiq as taslim (submission), which excludes rejection and arrogance, unlike mere knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I believe' (amantu), do you truly feel that your heart has made a voluntary, conscious affirmation of every article of faith, or are you merely repeating words without deep conviction? What would it take for your tasdiq to become more active and alive today?
?
The Prophet relied on the immediate understanding of tasdiq without lengthy explanation. What one step can you take this week to strengthen that instinctive tasdiq?
?
Sanusi emphasizes that iman is a commanded act, not passive knowledge. Are there areas of your life where you treat belief as mere intellectual agreement without letting it transform your choices? What would it look like to actively 'effect the relation' of your heart to Allah's commands starting today?

Iman: Distinct from Knowledge, Defined as Submission
Sanusi concludes by distinguishing iman from knowledge and citing Ghazali's definition of tasdiq as submission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that iman is tasdiq in specific matters, distinguished from mere knowledge, and that it is defined as submission (taslim) by scholars like Ghazali.

Core Idea
Faith is volitional submission, not just intellectual knowledge.

The author concludes by reiterating that iman is tasdiq of specific matters in the linguistic sense, expressed in Persian as 'karvidan' and 'rasti dashtan'. He stresses the difference from knowledge, quoting more Quranic verses to show that disbelievers knew the truth but did not affirm. Finally, he cites Imam al-Ghazali's interpretation of tasdiq as taslim (submission), which excludes arrogance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the clarification on transfer
The author acknowledges that if someone says iman was transferred to specific matters, there is no dispute. The key is it remains tasdiq in the linguistic sense.
2
Recognize the Persian equivalents
Words like 'karvidan' show the meaning is clear and not confused.
This indicates the concept is accessible to common people.
3
Study the Quranic proofs
Multiple verses show disbelievers had knowledge but not affirmation due to obstinacy. This demonstrates the need to distinguish between knowledge and tasdiq.
The distinction is crucial for the doctrine of iman.
4
Appreciate Ghazali's interpretation
Al-Ghazali interprets tasdiq as taslim (submission), which is incompatible with rejection and arrogance, unlike mere knowledge.
This defines faith as volitional submission.

ويقابله التكذيب وينافيه التردد، وهو غير العلم والمعرفة، لأن من الكفار من كان يعرف ولا يصدق. قال الله: الذين آتيناهم الكتاب يعرفونه كما يعرفون أبناءهم) (۱) وإن الذين أوتوا الكتاب ليعلمون أنه الحق (۲) وجحدوا بها واستيقنتها أنفسهم (۳). وبين الفرق بأن المقابل للتصديق الإنكار والتكذيب، وللمعرفة النكر والجهالة. ولهذا قد يفسر بالتسليم وبالعكس وبأن التصديق ربط القلب على ما علم من إخبار المخبر، وهو كسبي اختياري، ولهذا يؤمر به ويثاب عليه. والمعرفة ربما تحصل بلا كسب. ولقد زاد من قال المعتبر في الإيمان التصديق الاختياري. ومعناه نسبة الصدق إلى المتكلم اختياراً. وبهذا يمتاز عما جعل في المنطق مقابلاً للتصور فإنه قد يخلو عن الاختيار فلا يكون تصديقاً في اللغة، فلا يكون إيماناً في الشرع، كيف والتصديق مأمور به، فيكون فعلاً اختيارياً هو إيقاع النسبة اختياراً، والعلم كيفية نفسانية أو انفعال). في اللغة التصديق بشهادة النقل عن أئمة اللغة ودلالة موارد الاستعمال. ولم ينقل في الشرع إلى معنى آخر. أما أولاً، فلأن النقل خلاف الأصل لا يصار إليه إلا بدليل. وأما ثانياً، فلأنه كثر في الكتاب والسنة خطاب العرب به. بل كان ذلك أول الواجبات وأساس المشروعات، فامتثل من امتثل من غير استفسار ولا توقف إلى بيان ولم يكن ذلك من الخطاب بما لا يفهم وإنما احتيج إلى بيان ما يجب الإيمان به فبين وفصل بعض التفصيل، حيث قال النبي (عليه السلام) لمن سأله عن الإيمان: الإيمان أن تؤمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله... الحديث. فذكر لفظ تؤمن بالله تعويلاً على ظهور معناه عندهم. ثم قال: هذا جبرائيل أتاكم يعلمكم دينكم. ولو كان الإيمان غير التصديق، لما كان هذا تعليماً وإرشاداً، بل تلبساً وإضلالاً. نعم لو قيل إنه في اللغة لمطلق التصديق، وقد نقل في الشرع إلى التصديق بأمور مخصوصة، فلا نزاع. وإنما المقصود أنه تصديق بالأمور المخصوصة بالمعنى اللغوي، وهو ما يعبر عنه بالفارسية بكرويدن وراستكوي داشتن ويخالفه التكذيب، وينافيه التوقف والتردد. ولهذا اختار العلماء في ألفاظ الإيمان كرويدم باور داشتم راستكوي داشتم، بدل، وأنه معنى واضح عند العقل لا يشتبه على العوام، فضلاً عن الخواص والمذهب أنه غير العلم والمعرفة، لأن من الكفار من كان يعرف الحق ولا يصدق به عناداً واستكباراً. قال الله تعالى: الذين آتيناهم الكتاب يعرفونه كما يعرفون أبناءهم وإن فريقاً منهم ليكتمون الحق وهم يعلمون) (۱). وقال: وإن الذين أوتوا الكتاب ليعلمون أنه الحق من ربهم وما الله بغافل عما يعملون) (٢). وقال: وجحدوا بها واستيقنتها أنفسهم ظلماً وعلوا (۳) وقال حكاية عن موسى (عليه السلام) لفرعون ولقد علمت ما أنزل هؤلاء إلا رب السموات والأرض بصائر) (٤) فاحتيج إلى الفرق بين العلم بما جاء به النبي (عليه السلام) وهو معرفته، وبين التصديق ليصح كون الأول حاصلاً للمعاندين، دون الثاني، وكون الثاني إيماناً دون الأول. فاقتصر بعضهم على أن ضد التصديق هو الإنكار والتكذيب، وضد المعرفة النكارة والجهالة. وإليه أشار الإمام الغزالي (رحمه الله) حيث فسر التصديق بالتسليم فإنه لا يكون مع الإنكار والاستكبار، بخلاف العلم
And its opposite is takdhib (denial) and its contradictory is taraddud (hesitation), and it [tasdiq] is other than 'ilm (knowledge) and ma'rifa (cognition), because among the disbelievers were those who knew (ya'rifu) but did not affirm (yusaddiq). Allah said: 'Those to whom We gave the Book recognize it as they recognize their sons' (1) and 'Indeed those who were given the Book know that it is the truth' (2) and 'They denied them, though their souls were convinced of them' (3). And the difference [between tasdiq and ma'rifa] is explained: the opposite of tasdiq is inkar (rejection) and takdhib; the opposite of ma'rifa is nakara (ignorance) and jahala (ignorance). For this reason, it [tasdiq] may be interpreted as taslim (submission) and vice versa, and that tasdiq is the binding of the heart to what one knows from the informant's report, and it is acquired and voluntary (kashbi ikhtiyari), and therefore one is commanded to do it and rewarded for it. But ma'rifa may be obtained without acquisition. And indeed he who said that the criterion in iman (faith) is ikhtiyari tasdiq (voluntary affirmation) has added [something]. Its meaning is ascribing truthfulness to the speaker voluntarily. By this it is distinguished from what is made in logic as the counterpart of tasawwur (conception), for it may be devoid of choice, so it would not be tasdiq in language, so it would not be iman in the Shari'a. How [could it be]? And tasdiq is commanded, so it is a voluntary act, which is effecting the relation voluntarily, while 'ilm is a psychical quality or passion. In language, tasdiq [is proven] by the testimony of transmission from the imams of language and the indication of contexts of usage. And it was not transferred in the Shari'a to another meaning. As for first, because transfer is contrary to the principle, and recourse is not made to it except with evidence. As for second, because in the Book and the Sunnah the address to the Arabs with it is frequent. Rather it was the first of obligations and the foundation of legislated matters, so those who complied did so without inquiry or hesitation for explanation, and that was not an address with what is not understood, but rather there was need to explain what must be believed in, so he explained and detailed some detail, when the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the one who asked him about iman: 'Iman is that you believe (tu'min) in Allah, His angels, His books, and His messengers...' the hadith. So he mentioned the word tu'min (you believe) relying on the clearness of its meaning among them. Then he said: 'This is Jibril, he came to teach you your religion.' And if iman were other than tasdiq, this would not be teaching and guidance, but rather confusion and misguidance. Yes, if it is said that it [iman] in language is absolute tasdiq, and in the Shari'a it was transferred to tasdiq of specific matters, then there is no dispute. Rather the intended meaning is that it is tasdiq of the specific matters in the linguistic sense, which is expressed in Persian as 'karvidan' and 'rasti dashtan', and it is opposed by takdhib, and its contradictory is tawquf (stopping) and taraddud. And therefore scholars chose in the expressions of iman: 'karvidam', 'bawur dashtam', 'rasti dashtam', instead, and that it is a meaning clear in the intellect, not confused for the common people, let alone the elite. And the doctrine is that it [iman] is other than 'ilm and ma'rifa, because among the disbelievers were those who knew the truth but did not affirm it out of obstinacy and arrogance. Allah Almighty said: 'Those to whom We gave the Book recognize it as they recognize their sons, and indeed a party of them conceal the truth while they know' (1). And He said: 'And indeed those who were given the Book know that it is the truth from their Lord, and Allah is not unaware of what they do' (2). And He said: 'And they denied them [the signs], though their souls were convinced of them, out of injustice and haughtiness' (3). And He related from Moses (peace be upon him) to Pharaoh: 'And you certainly know that none has sent down these [signs] except the Lord of the heavens and the earth as insights' (4). So there was need to distinguish between knowledge of what the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought—which is ma'rifa of it—and tasdiq, so that it is correct that the former is possessed by the obstinate, but not the latter, and that the latter is iman and not the former. So some confined themselves [to saying] that the opposite of tasdiq is inkar and takdhib, and the opposite of ma'rifa is nakara and jahala. And Imam al-Ghazali (may Allah have mercy on him) alluded to this where he interpreted tasdiq as taslim, for it does not accompany inkar and istikbar (arrogance), unlike 'ilm.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage defines tasdiq (affirmation/assent) as the core of iman (faith) and distinguishes it sharply from 'ilm or ma'rifa (knowledge/cognition). The author begins by stating that tasdiq is opposed by takdhib (denial) and contradictory to taraddud (hesitation). It is not the same as knowledge, because many disbelievers had knowledge of the truth—as shown by Quranic verses—yet did not affirm it. The key difference is that the opposite of tasdiq is inkar (rejection) and takdhib, while the opposite of ma'rifa is nakara (ignorance) and jahala. Tasdiq is an acquired, voluntary act (kashbi ikhtiyari); it is binding the heart to what one knows from the informant, and it is commanded and rewarded. In contrast, ma'rifa may occur without any voluntary acquisition. The author then emphasizes that the criterion in iman is voluntary tasdiq (ikhtari tasdiq), meaning ascribing truthfulness to the speaker by choice. This distinguishes it from the logical term 'tasdiq' which is the counterpart of tasawwur (conception) and may be involuntary; such involuntary assent would not be tasdiq in the linguistic sense, and thus not iman in the Shari'a. The author then provides proof from language and revelation that the term 'iman' in the Shari'a retains its linguistic meaning of tasdiq, not transferred to a new meaning. He argues that transfer is contrary to the default principle and requires evidence, and that the Quran and Sunnah frequently address the Arabs with this word without needing explanation—indeed, the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Jibril defined iman as 'to believe in Allah...' relying on the clear meaning of 'tu'min' (you believe). If iman were not tasdiq, this teaching would be confusing rather than instructive. The author then notes that if someone claims that iman in language is absolute tasdiq but in Shari'a it is tasdiq of specific matters, then there is no real dispute; the intended meaning is that iman is tasdiq of those specific matters in the linguistic sense, expressed in Persian as 'karvidan' and 'rasti dashtan'. He reiterates the doctrine that iman is distinct from mere knowledge, citing Quranic verses showing that disbelievers had knowledge but not affirmation due to obstinacy. Thus a distinction is necessary: ma'rifa can coexist with obstinacy, but tasdiq cannot. Some scholars have therefore defined tasdiq as taslim (submission), which excludes rejection and arrogance, unlike mere knowledge.

Correction: The author shows that submission (taslim) is essential, as per Ghazali's interpretation.

Key Takeaway
Iman is volitional tasdiq of specific truths, distinct from knowledge, and is essentially submission (taslim).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know the truth of Islam in your mind. But where in your life are you still holding back submission? What area of your obedience is still marked by arrogance rather than taslim?
?
The disbelievers knew the truth but rejected it out of obstinacy. What small act of rebellion in your heart today is a form of that same inkar? Will you name it and repent?
?
If iman is taslim, then what part of your life are you still negotiating with Allah instead of surrendering? Will you commit to submitting fully right now, without conditions?

Definition of Tasdiq and Its Distinction from Ma'rifa
The author defines tasdiq and distinguishes it from ma'rifa, emphasizing its voluntary nature for iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of tasdiq as an acquired act of the heart binding to a reporter's information, and how it differs from knowledge (ma'rifa) which can occur involuntarily.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is a voluntary heart-binding, not mere knowledge.

In this passage, the author establishes the foundational concept of tasdiq (assent) as it relates to faith. He distinguishes it from simple knowledge (ma'rifa), which can occur without choice, by emphasizing that true tasdiq is a commanded, rewarded act that forms the head of worship. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the nature of iman.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage carefully, noting the key terms: تصديق, معرفة, اختيار. The translation will help clarify the meaning.
2
Identify the definition and contrast
Find where the author defines tasdiq as 'binding of the heart' and then contrasts it with ma'rifa. Notice that tasdiq is acquired (kasbi) and rewarded, while ma'rifa can be involuntary.
The example of seeing a wall illustrates involuntary knowledge.
3
Understand the restriction to voluntary
The later scholar restricts the tasdiq required for iman to voluntary attribution of truth. This distinguishes it from logical tasdiq, which can be involuntary, as in the example of the prophet and the miracle.
The sophist and the disbeliever know but do not voluntarily assent.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
. التصديق والمعرفة. وفصل بعضهم زيادة تفصيل وقال : التصديق عبارة عن ربط القلب بما علم من إخبار المخبر، وهو أمر كسبي يثبت باخبار المصدق ولهذا يؤمر ويثاب عليه بل يجعل رأس العبادات بخلاف المعرفة فإنها ربما يحصل بلا كسب كمن وقع بصره على جسم فحصل له معرفة أنه جدار أو حجر، وحققه بعض المتأخرين زيادة تحقيق، فقال : المعتبر في الإيمان هو الاختياري ومعناه نسبة الصدق إلى المتكلم اختياراً. وبهذا القيد يمتاز عن التصديق المنطقي المقابل للتصور. فإنه قد يخلو عن الاختيار. كما إذا ادعى النبي النبوة، وأظهر المعجزة، فوقع في القلب صدقه ضرورة من غير أن ينسب إليه اختياراً، فإنه لا يقال في اللغة إنه صدقه فلا يكون إيماناً شرعياً. كيف، والتصديق مأمور به فيكون فعلاً اختيارياً زائداً على العلم لكونه كيفية نفسانية أو انفعالاً وهو حصول المعنى في القلب والفعل القلبي ليس كذلك. بل هو إيقاع النسبة اختياراً الذي هو كلام النفس ويسمى عقد القلب. فالسوفسطائي عالم بوجود النهار ، وكذا بعض الكفار بنبوة النبي عليه السلام لكنهم ليسوا مصدقين لغة، لأنهم لا يحكمون اختياراً، بل ينكرون . وكلام هذا المحقق متردد يميل تارة إلى أن التصديق المعتبر في الإيمان نوع من التصديق المنطقي الذي هو أحد قسمي العلم لكونه مقيداً بالاختيار وكون التصديق العلمي أعم لا فرق بينهما إلا بلزوم الاختيار ،وعدمه وتارة إلى أنه ليس من جنس العلم أصلاً لكونه فعلاً اختيارياً ، وكون العلم كيفية أو انفعالاً. وعلى هذا الأخير أصر بعض المعتنين بتحقيق معنى الإيمان، وجزم بأن التسليم الذي فسر به الإمام الغزالي التصديق ليس من جنس العلم، بل أمر وراء معناه كردن دادن و كرويدن و حق داشتن مرانداكه حق دانسته باشى ويؤيده ما ذكر إمام الحرمين أن التصديق على التحقيق كلام النفس، لكن لا يثبت كلام النفس إلا مع العلم .
Assent (al-tasdiq) and knowledge (al-ma'rifa). And some of them detailed further and said: al-tasdiq is an expression for the binding of the heart to what is known from the report of the reporter, and it is an acquired matter (kasbi) established by the report of the one assented to, and for this reason it is commanded and rewarded, rather it is made the head of acts of worship, unlike knowledge, for it may sometimes occur without acquisition, like one whose sight falls upon a body and he gains knowledge that it is a wall or a stone. And a later scholar verified it with extra verification and said: the considered element in faith (al-iman) is the voluntary (al-ikhtiyari), and its meaning is the attribution of truthfulness to the speaker voluntarily. And by this restriction it is distinguished from logical assent (al-tasdiq al-mantiqi) opposite of conception (al-tasawwur), for it may lack choice. As when the Prophet claims prophethood and performs a miracle, and truthfulness falls into the heart necessarily without being attributed to him voluntarily, for it is not said in the language that he assented to him, so it would not be legal faith. How? And assent is commanded, so it is a voluntary act additional to knowledge, because it is a psychic quality (kayfiyya nafsaniyya) or a passivity (infi'al), which is the occurrence of the meaning in the heart, and the mental act is not like that. Rather it is the voluntary positing of the relation, which is speech of the soul (kalam al-nafs) and is called the heart's contract ('aqd al-qalb). So the sophist (al-sufasta'i) knows the existence of daytime, and likewise some disbelievers [know] the prophethood of the Prophet (peace be upon him), but they are not assenters linguistically, because they do not judge voluntarily, rather they deny. And the speech of this verifier is hesitant, inclining sometimes to the view that the assent considered in faith is a type of logical assent which is one of the two divisions of knowledge, because it is restricted by choice, and that scientific assent is more general, no difference between them except by the necessity of choice and its absence, and sometimes to the view that it is not of the genus of knowledge at all, because it is a voluntary act, and that knowledge is a quality or a passivity. And on this latter view, some of those concerned with verifying the meaning of faith insisted, and affirmed that the submission (al-taslim) with which Imam al-Ghazali interpreted assent is not of the genus of knowledge, but something beyond its meaning: 'kardan dādan wa krawīdan wa ḥaq dāshtan mar ān rā ki ḥaq dānista bāshī'. And it is supported by what Imam al-Haramayn mentioned: that assent in reality is speech of the soul, but speech of the soul is not established except with knowledge.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage defines tasdiq (assent) and distinguishes it from ma'rifa (knowledge), establishing that the tasdiq required for iman (faith) is a voluntary act of the heart, not mere knowledge. The author begins by stating the topic: 'Assent and knowledge.' He then reports a detailed classification by some scholars: tasdiq is the binding of the heart to what is known from a reporter's report; it is acquired (kasbi) and therefore commanded and rewarded, unlike knowledge which can occur involuntarily. A later scholar clarifies that the considered element in iman is the voluntary (ikhtiyari) attribution of truth to the speaker. This distinguishes it from logical tasdiq, which can be involuntary—as when someone necessarily knows a prophet is truthful but does not voluntarily affirm it, thus not being called 'saddaqa' (he assented) linguistically, and hence not iman. The author explains that tasdiq is commanded, so it must be a voluntary act additional to knowledge; it is a psychic quality or passivity, but the mental act (al-fi'l al-qalbi) is the voluntary positing of the relation, called 'speech of the soul' (kalam al-nafs) or 'heart's contract' ('aqd al-qalb). Examples: the sophist knows daytime, some disbelievers know the Prophet's truthfulness, but they do not assent voluntarily—they deny. The verifier's view oscillates between considering this tasdiq a type of logical tasdiq (a division of knowledge) with the added condition of choice, and considering it not knowledge at all but a voluntary act. The latter view is insisted upon by some, who affirm that al-Ghazali's 'taslim' is beyond knowledge, and is supported by Imam al-Haramayn's statement that tasdiq is speech of the soul, but speech of the soul is not established except with knowledge.

معرفة

عقد القلب

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some confuse logical tasdiq (which can be involuntary) with the tasdiq required for iman, which must be voluntary.
Correction: The passage clarifies that iman requires voluntary attribution of truth, not mere involuntary recognition.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq for iman is a voluntary act of the heart, not just involuntary knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever simply 'known' something about Islam to be true but felt a resistance in your heart to fully embrace it? What would it mean for you to move from mere knowledge to a voluntary, heart-binding assent today?
?
If the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood before you and you witnessed a miracle, would your heart automatically yield or would you still need to make a conscious choice to affirm his truthfulness? Where do you feel that voluntary choice in your own iman?
?
The passage says tasdiq is the 'head of acts of worship.' Is your prayer, fasting, and charity flowing from a voluntary inner contract with Allah, or are they hollow habits built on knowledge without heart engagement? What one step can you take this week to renew that inner contract?

The Voluntary Nature of Tasdiq: Debate on Its Essence
The author presents the debate on whether tasdiq is a type of knowledge or a distinct voluntary act, supporting the latter view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly debate on whether the tasdiq required for iman is a type of knowledge conditioned by choice or a completely distinct voluntary act.

Core Idea
True tasdiq is a voluntary act of the heart, beyond mere knowledge.

After establishing that tasdiq must be voluntary for iman, the author presents a scholarly debate about its precise nature. Some view it as a type of logical tasdiq with the added condition of choice, while others argue it is not knowledge at all but a separate voluntary act. This lesson examines both positions and the evidence provided for the latter view, including references to al-Ghazali and Imam al-Haramayn.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the debate
Carefully read the Arabic and translation, which present the verifier's hesitation between two views and the subsequent support for the second view.
2
Identify the two opinions
The verifier's speech inclines to two opinions: (1) tasdiq is a type of logical tasdiq (a division of knowledge) restricted by choice, (2) tasdiq is not knowledge at all but a voluntary act. Note the key phrases: 'نوع من التصديق المنطقي' and 'ليس من جنس العلم أصلاً'.
3
Understand the support for the second opinion
Some scholars insist that al-Ghazali's 'taslim' is beyond knowledge, and Imam al-Haramayn says tasdiq is speech of the soul, which requires knowledge but is not identical. Reflect on the Persian phrase and its meaning.
The Persian phrase emphasizes heart-felt submission.

. التصديق والمعرفة. وفصل بعضهم زيادة تفصيل وقال : التصديق عبارة عن ربط القلب بما علم من إخبار المخبر، وهو أمر كسبي يثبت باخبار المصدق ولهذا يؤمر ويثاب عليه بل يجعل رأس العبادات بخلاف المعرفة فإنها ربما يحصل بلا كسب كمن وقع بصره على جسم فحصل له معرفة أنه جدار أو حجر، وحققه بعض المتأخرين زيادة تحقيق، فقال : المعتبر في الإيمان هو الاختياري ومعناه نسبة الصدق إلى المتكلم اختياراً. وبهذا القيد يمتاز عن التصديق المنطقي المقابل للتصور. فإنه قد يخلو عن الاختيار. كما إذا ادعى النبي النبوة، وأظهر المعجزة، فوقع في القلب صدقه ضرورة من غير أن ينسب إليه اختياراً، فإنه لا يقال في اللغة إنه صدقه فلا يكون إيماناً شرعياً. كيف، والتصديق مأمور به فيكون فعلاً اختيارياً زائداً على العلم لكونه كيفية نفسانية أو انفعالاً وهو حصول المعنى في القلب والفعل القلبي ليس كذلك. بل هو إيقاع النسبة اختياراً الذي هو كلام النفس ويسمى عقد القلب. فالسوفسطائي عالم بوجود النهار ، وكذا بعض الكفار بنبوة النبي عليه السلام لكنهم ليسوا مصدقين لغة، لأنهم لا يحكمون اختياراً، بل ينكرون . وكلام هذا المحقق متردد يميل تارة إلى أن التصديق المعتبر في الإيمان نوع من التصديق المنطقي الذي هو أحد قسمي العلم لكونه مقيداً بالاختيار وكون التصديق العلمي أعم لا فرق بينهما إلا بلزوم الاختيار ،وعدمه وتارة إلى أنه ليس من جنس العلم أصلاً لكونه فعلاً اختيارياً ، وكون العلم كيفية أو انفعالاً. وعلى هذا الأخير أصر بعض المعتنين بتحقيق معنى الإيمان، وجزم بأن التسليم الذي فسر به الإمام الغزالي التصديق ليس من جنس العلم، بل أمر وراء معناه كردن دادن و كرويدن و حق داشتن مرانداكه حق دانسته باشى ويؤيده ما ذكر إمام الحرمين أن التصديق على التحقيق كلام النفس، لكن لا يثبت كلام النفس إلا مع العلم .
Assent (al-tasdiq) and knowledge (al-ma'rifa). And some of them detailed further and said: al-tasdiq is an expression for the binding of the heart to what is known from the report of the reporter, and it is an acquired matter (kasbi) established by the report of the one assented to, and for this reason it is commanded and rewarded, rather it is made the head of acts of worship, unlike knowledge, for it may sometimes occur without acquisition, like one whose sight falls upon a body and he gains knowledge that it is a wall or a stone. And a later scholar verified it with extra verification and said: the considered element in faith (al-iman) is the voluntary (al-ikhtiyari), and its meaning is the attribution of truthfulness to the speaker voluntarily. And by this restriction it is distinguished from logical assent (al-tasdiq al-mantiqi) opposite of conception (al-tasawwur), for it may lack choice. As when the Prophet claims prophethood and performs a miracle, and truthfulness falls into the heart necessarily without being attributed to him voluntarily, for it is not said in the language that he assented to him, so it would not be legal faith. How? And assent is commanded, so it is a voluntary act additional to knowledge, because it is a psychic quality (kayfiyya nafsaniyya) or a passivity (infi'al), which is the occurrence of the meaning in the heart, and the mental act is not like that. Rather it is the voluntary positing of the relation, which is speech of the soul (kalam al-nafs) and is called the heart's contract ('aqd al-qalb). So the sophist (al-sufasta'i) knows the existence of daytime, and likewise some disbelievers [know] the prophethood of the Prophet (peace be upon him), but they are not assenters linguistically, because they do not judge voluntarily, rather they deny. And the speech of this verifier is hesitant, inclining sometimes to the view that the assent considered in faith is a type of logical assent which is one of the two divisions of knowledge, because it is restricted by choice, and that scientific assent is more general, no difference between them except by the necessity of choice and its absence, and sometimes to the view that it is not of the genus of knowledge at all, because it is a voluntary act, and that knowledge is a quality or a passivity. And on this latter view, some of those concerned with verifying the meaning of faith insisted, and affirmed that the submission (al-taslim) with which Imam al-Ghazali interpreted assent is not of the genus of knowledge, but something beyond its meaning: 'kardan dādan wa krawīdan wa ḥaq dāshtan mar ān rā ki ḥaq dānista bāshī'. And it is supported by what Imam al-Haramayn mentioned: that assent in reality is speech of the soul, but speech of the soul is not established except with knowledge.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage defines tasdiq (assent) and distinguishes it from ma'rifa (knowledge), establishing that the tasdiq required for iman (faith) is a voluntary act of the heart, not mere knowledge. The author begins by stating the topic: 'Assent and knowledge.' He then reports a detailed classification by some scholars: tasdiq is the binding of the heart to what is known from a reporter's report; it is acquired (kasbi) and therefore commanded and rewarded, unlike knowledge which can occur involuntarily. A later scholar clarifies that the considered element in iman is the voluntary (ikhtiyari) attribution of truth to the speaker. This distinguishes it from logical tasdiq, which can be involuntary—as when someone necessarily knows a prophet is truthful but does not voluntarily affirm it, thus not being called 'saddaqa' (he assented) linguistically, and hence not iman. The author explains that tasdiq is commanded, so it must be a voluntary act additional to knowledge; it is a psychic quality or passivity, but the mental act (al-fi'l al-qalbi) is the voluntary positing of the relation, called 'speech of the soul' (kalam al-nafs) or 'heart's contract' ('aqd al-qalb). Examples: the sophist knows daytime, some disbelievers know the Prophet's truthfulness, but they do not assent voluntarily—they deny. The verifier's view oscillates between considering this tasdiq a type of logical tasdiq (a division of knowledge) with the added condition of choice, and considering it not knowledge at all but a voluntary act. The latter view is insisted upon by some, who affirm that al-Ghazali's 'taslim' is beyond knowledge, and is supported by Imam al-Haramayn's statement that tasdiq is speech of the soul, but speech of the soul is not established except with knowledge.

Key Terms
تصديق
اختيار
تسليم
كلام النفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that tasdiq is simply knowledge, without any additional voluntary act.
Correction: The passage shows that many scholars argue tasdiq is a voluntary act beyond knowledge, as seen in the example of the sophist who knows but does not assent.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first opinion about the tasdiq considered in faith?
A) It is a voluntary act distinct from knowledge.
B) It is a type of logical tasdiq, a division of knowledge, restricted by choice.
C) It is identical to ma'rifa.
D) It is the same as taslim.

Key Takeaway
The tasdiq required for iman is not mere knowledge; it is a voluntary act of the heart, supported by the views of al-Ghazali and Imam al-Haramayn.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that Allah exists and that Islam is true, but have you ever truly submitted your heart to that truth in a voluntary act, or do you merely possess knowledge that does not move you to action? What would it take for you to move from knowing to taslim?
?
When you reflect on your own iman, do you find that your tasdiq is a passive awareness or an active, chosen commitment? Which of the two views in this passage describes your current state, and what can you do to cultivate the voluntary assent that the scholars emphasised?
?
The passage mentions that tasdiq is 'speech of the soul' that requires knowledge but goes beyond it. In your daily life, does your inner speech affirm what you know, or do you sometimes hold back from full submission? What is one area where you can consciously choose to submit your heart today?

The Logical Definition of Tasdiq and Its Distinction from Linguistic Tasdiq
Avicenna's definition of logical tasdiq and its contrast with linguistic tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise logical definition of tasdiq (assent) as defined by Avicenna and how it differs from its ordinary linguistic meaning.

Core Idea
Logical tasdiq is the mind’s correspondence judgment, not mere verbal affirmation.

In this passage, the author begins by clarifying that the term 'tasdiq' in logic is not the same as in ordinary language. He cites Avicenna's al-Shifa to give a technical definition: tasdiq is not just having a complete proposition in mind, but the mind's relating that proposition to external reality with correspondence. This distinction is crucial because it affects how we understand the role of tasdiq in knowledge and faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the definition.
Notice the key term 'Kruwidan' which is the Persian equivalent.
2
Identify the Avicennan definition
Locate the sentences where Avicenna defines tasdiq. Note that it involves a relation of correspondence between the mental proposition and external reality.
3
Contrast with common understanding
The author explicitly says tasdiq is not merely 'the occurrence of the complete relation in the mind' as some think. Understand the nuance.
4
Understand the opposition to takdhib
He explains tasdiq as 'true-holding' and takdhib as 'false-holding'. This clarifies the logical sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أن «كرويدن» في المنطق غيره في اللغة. وقال في الشفاء : التصديق في قولك البياض عرض هو أن يحصل في الذهن نسبة صورة هذا التأليف إلى الأشياء أنفسها أنها مطابقة لها والتكذيب يخالف ذلك. فلم يجعل التصديق حصول النسبة التامة في الذهن على ما يفهمه البعض بل حصول أن ينسب الذهن الثبوت أو الانتفاء الذي بين طرفي التأليف إلى ما في نفس الأمر بالمطابقة . ومعناه نسبة الحكم إلى الصدق أعني صادق داشتن) وكرويدن وبينه بأنه ضد التكذيب الذي معناه النسبة إلى الكذب. أعني كاذب داشتن . وبهذا يندفع ما يقال إن الحكم فعل اختياري هو الإيقاع أو الانتزاع، فكيف يكون نفس التصديق أو جزءه . والتصديق قسم من العلم الذي هو من مقولة الكيف أو الانفعال ونعم ما قال من قال : الإسناد والإيقاع، ونحو ذلك، ألفاظ وعبارات والتحقيق أنه ليس للنفس ههنا تأثير وفعل. بل إذعان وقبول وإدراك أن النسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعة. نعم، حصول هذا التصديق قد يكون بالكسب أي مباشرة الأسباب بالاختيار كإلقاء الذهن وصرف النظر، وتوجيه الحواس وما أشبه ذلك. وقد يكون بدونه كمن وقع عليه الضوء فعلم أن الشمس طالعة . والمأمور به يجب أن يكون من الأول.

فإن قيل : فاليقين الحاصل بدون الإذعان والقبول، بل مع الجحود والاستكبار كما للسوفسطائي، ولبعض الكفار يكون من قبيل التصور دون التصديق . وهو ظاهر البطلان .

قلنا : نحن لا ندعي إلا كون التصديق المنطقي على ما يفسره رئيسهم، لا على ما يفهمه كل نساج وحلاج هو التصديق اللغوي، المقابل للتكذيب المعبر عنه «بكرويدن». وأنه لا يصح حينئذ إطلاق القول وإطباق القوم على أن المعتبر في الإيمان هو اللغوي، دون المنطقي. بل غايته أن يجب اشتراط أمور كالاختيار وترك الجحود والاستكبار. وأما أنه يلزم على قصد تقسيمه وتفسيره كون اليقين الخالي عن الإذعان والقبول تصوراً أو خارجاً عن التصور (۱)

(1) التصور حصول صورة الشيء في الذهن ، وقيل : هو إدراك الماهية من غير أن يحكم عليها بنفي أو إثبات .

والتصديق، فذلك بحث آخر. لكن الكلام في إمكان الإيقان بدل الإذعان، وفي كون بعض الكفار موقنين بجميع ما جاء به النبي عليه السلام) غير مصدقين وفي أن كفرهم ليس من جهة الإباء عن الإقرار باللسان والاستكبار عن امتثال الأوامر، وقبول الأحكام والإصرار على التكذيب باللسان، إلى غير موجبات الكفر، مع تصديق القلب لعدم الاعتداد به مع تلك الأمارات، كما في إلقاء المصحف في القاذورات.
That 'Kruwidan' in logic is different from it in language. And he said in al-Shifa: Tasdiq in your statement 'whiteness is an accident' is that there occurs in the mind a relation of the form of this composition to the things themselves that it corresponds to them, and takdhib (denial) is the opposite of that. So he did not make tasdiq the occurrence of the complete relation in the mind as some understand, but rather the occurrence that the mind relates the affirmation or negation that is between the two sides of the composition to what is in external reality by correspondence. And its meaning is relating the judgment to truth, i.e., 'true-holding' (ṣādiq dāshtan), and Kruwidan, and he explained it as the opposite of takdhib, whose meaning is relating to falsehood, i.e., 'false-holding' (kādhib dāshtan). And by this is repelled what is said: 'Judgment is a voluntary act, which is the positing or abstraction, so how can it be the same as tasdiq or a part of it?' And tasdiq is a division of knowledge, which belongs to the category of quality or passion. And excellent is what he who said said: 'al-isnād (attribution) and al-īqā' (positing), and the like, are words and expressions. And the truth is that there is for the soul here no effect and act, but rather acquiescence (idh'ān), acceptance (qubūl), and perception (idrāk) that the relation is existent or not existent. Yes, the attainment of this tasdiq may be through acquisition (al-kasb), i.e., directly employing causes by choice, such as directing the mind, focusing attention, directing the senses, and the like. And it may be without that, like one upon whom light falls and he knows that the sun is rising. And what is commanded must be of the first kind. If it is said: 'Then certainty (al-yaqīn) obtained without acquiescence and acceptance, but rather with denial (juhūd) and arrogance (istikbār), as for the sophist and some unbelievers, would be of the kind of tasawwur (conception) without tasdiq, and that is obviously false.' We say: We do not claim except that logical tasdiq, as their leader interprets it—not as every weaver and carder understands it—is linguistic tasdiq, the counterpart of takdhib expressed by 'Kruwidan'. And that it is not valid then to make a definitive statement and the consensus of the people that what is considered in faith is the linguistic, not the logical. Rather, its utmost is that conditions must be stipulated such as choice (ikhtiyār) and abandoning denial and arrogance. As for the claim that it follows from the intention of its division and interpretation that certainty devoid of acquiescence and acceptance is a tasawwur or outside of tasawwur, that is another discussion. But the discussion is about the possibility of certainty instead of acquiescence, and about some unbelievers being certain of all that the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought without being musaddiqīn (affirmers), and that their unbelief is not from refusal of verbal acknowledgment and arrogance about obeying commands, accepting judgments, and persistence in verbal denial, up to other causes of unbelief, while having tasdiq of the heart, because it is not regarded with those indications, as in throwing the Quran into filth.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage defines tasdiq (assent) and addresses an objection. The author first distinguishes the logical term 'Kruwidan' (assent) from its linguistic meaning, citing Avicenna's al-Shifa. In logic, tasdiq is the mind's relating a judgment to reality with correspondence—not merely having the complete proposition in mind. It is explained as 'true-holding' (ṣādiq dāshtan), opposed to takdhib ('false-holding'). This definition repels the claim that judgment is a voluntary act (like positing or abstraction) and thus cannot be tasdiq or its part. The truth is that tasdiq is a kind of knowledge in the category of quality or passion; the soul merely acquiesces, accepts, and perceives the relation. Its attainment may be through voluntary acquisition or involuntarily. The commanded (in faith) must be acquired voluntarily. An objection arises: certainty without acquiescence (as in sophists) would be only conception (tasawwur), not tasdiq—which is false. The answer clarifies that logical tasdiq as defined by the logicians is different from the linguistic tasdiq used in faith. The scholars' agreement that linguistic tasdiq is what matters in faith is not undermined; it only requires additional conditions like choice. The objection about certainty without acquiescence is a separate discussion. However, the real issue is whether such certainty can substitute for acquiescence, and whether some unbelievers have certainty but not tasdiq—their unbelief stems from outward denial, not from lack of heart-tasdiq, which is disregarded due to contradictory signs (like throwing the Quran in filth).

Key Terms
تصديق
تکذيب
تصور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tasdiq is simply uttering a statement or having a proposition in mind.
Correction: Avicenna clarifies that logical tasdiq requires the mind to relate the judgment to external reality with correspondence, not merely to have the proposition in mind.

Checkpoint
According to Avicenna's definition in the passage, what distinguishes logical tasdiq from merely having a complete proposition in mind?
A) Tasdiq is the verbal pronunciation of the proposition.
B) Tasdiq involves the mind relating the proposition to external reality with correspondence.
C) Tasdiq is the same as the proposition itself.
D) Tasdiq is only concerned with inner feelings.

Key Takeaway
Logical tasdiq is a correspondence judgment, not a mere mental representation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I believe in God', are you merely voicing a proposition you've held in mind, or is there a real judgment in your heart that this truth corresponds to reality? How often do you examine the difference?
?
Think of one truth you profess verbally but rarely live as if it were real. What would change in your daily life if you truly 'held it as true' (ṣādiq dāshtan) in the way Avicenna describes?
?
If your faith is only a mental proposition—a thought you've heard and repeated—what would it take for you to transform it into a correspondence judgment that reshapes how you see every situation? Will you today ask yourself, 'Do I really affirm this as true about reality, or just about my mind?'

The Nature of Tasdiq: Acquiescence, Not a Voluntary Act
Author refutes the claim that tasdiq is a voluntary act and explains its nature as passive acquiescence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's argument that tasdiq is not a voluntary act of judgment but rather a passive state of acquiescence, and how it can be attained either voluntarily or involuntarily.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is not something the soul does; it is something the soul undergoes.

After defining tasdiq logically, the author addresses a potential objection: if judgment is a voluntary act (like positing or abstraction), how can it be the same as tasdiq? He argues that tasdiq is actually a kind of knowledge in the category of quality or passion—the soul does not act but rather acquiesces, accepts, and perceives. He then explains that the attainment of tasdiq can be through voluntary means (acquisition) or involuntary, but the commanded tasdiq in faith must be voluntary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the objection and response.
2
Identify the objection
Find the sentence that presents the objection: 'Judgment is a voluntary act...' Note the terms used (īqā' or intizā').
3
Understand the author's response
The author says this objection is repelled by the definition. He asserts that tasdiq is from the category of quality or passion, not an act. Look for the key phrase 'lāta'athīr wa lā fi'l'. Then he gives the two modes of attainment.
4
Distinguish voluntary and involuntary attainment
Identify the two ways tasdiq is attained: through kasb (acquisition) by choice, or without it. Notice the example of light and knowing the sun is rising.
5
Note the implication for faith
The last sentence states that what is commanded (i.e., faith) must be of the first kind (voluntary).
