فإن قيل : فاليقين الحاصل بدون الإذعان والقبول، بل مع الجحود والاستكبار كما للسوفسطائي، ولبعض الكفار يكون من قبيل التصور دون التصديق . وهو ظاهر البطلان .

قلنا : نحن لا ندعي إلا كون التصديق المنطقي على ما يفسره رئيسهم، لا على ما يفهمه كل نساج وحلاج هو التصديق اللغوي، المقابل للتكذيب المعبر عنه «بكرويدن». وأنه لا يصح حينئذ إطلاق القول وإطباق القوم على أن المعتبر في الإيمان هو اللغوي، دون المنطقي. بل غايته أن يجب اشتراط أمور كالاختيار وترك الجحود والاستكبار. وأما أنه يلزم على قصد تقسيمه وتفسيره كون اليقين الخالي عن الإذعان والقبول تصوراً أو خارجاً عن التصور (۱)

(1) التصور حصول صورة الشيء في الذهن ، وقيل : هو إدراك الماهية من غير أن يحكم عليها بنفي أو إثبات .

والتصديق، فذلك بحث آخر. لكن الكلام في إمكان الإيقان بدل الإذعان، وفي كون بعض الكفار موقنين بجميع ما جاء به النبي عليه السلام) غير مصدقين وفي أن كفرهم ليس من جهة الإباء عن الإقرار باللسان والاستكبار عن امتثال الأوامر، وقبول الأحكام والإصرار على التكذيب باللسان، إلى غير موجبات الكفر، مع تصديق القلب لعدم الاعتداد به مع تلك الأمارات، كما في إلقاء المصحف في القاذورات.
That 'Kruwidan' in logic is different from it in language. And he said in al-Shifa: Tasdiq in your statement 'whiteness is an accident' is that there occurs in the mind a relation of the form of this composition to the things themselves that it corresponds to them, and takdhib (denial) is the opposite of that. So he did not make tasdiq the occurrence of the complete relation in the mind as some understand, but rather the occurrence that the mind relates the affirmation or negation that is between the two sides of the composition to what is in external reality by correspondence. And its meaning is relating the judgment to truth, i.e., 'true-holding' (ṣādiq dāshtan), and Kruwidan, and he explained it as the opposite of takdhib, whose meaning is relating to falsehood, i.e., 'false-holding' (kādhib dāshtan). And by this is repelled what is said: 'Judgment is a voluntary act, which is the positing or abstraction, so how can it be the same as tasdiq or a part of it?' And tasdiq is a division of knowledge, which belongs to the category of quality or passion. And excellent is what he who said said: 'al-isnād (attribution) and al-īqā' (positing), and the like, are words and expressions. And the truth is that there is for the soul here no effect and act, but rather acquiescence (idh'ān), acceptance (qubūl), and perception (idrāk) that the relation is existent or not existent. Yes, the attainment of this tasdiq may be through acquisition (al-kasb), i.e., directly employing causes by choice, such as directing the mind, focusing attention, directing the senses, and the like. And it may be without that, like one upon whom light falls and he knows that the sun is rising. And what is commanded must be of the first kind. If it is said: 'Then certainty (al-yaqīn) obtained without acquiescence and acceptance, but rather with denial (juhūd) and arrogance (istikbār), as for the sophist and some unbelievers, would be of the kind of tasawwur (conception) without tasdiq, and that is obviously false.' We say: We do not claim except that logical tasdiq, as their leader interprets it—not as every weaver and carder understands it—is linguistic tasdiq, the counterpart of takdhib expressed by 'Kruwidan'. And that it is not valid then to make a definitive statement and the consensus of the people that what is considered in faith is the linguistic, not the logical. Rather, its utmost is that conditions must be stipulated such as choice (ikhtiyār) and abandoning denial and arrogance. As for the claim that it follows from the intention of its division and interpretation that certainty devoid of acquiescence and acceptance is a tasawwur or outside of tasawwur, that is another discussion. But the discussion is about the possibility of certainty instead of acquiescence, and about some unbelievers being certain of all that the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought without being musaddiqīn (affirmers), and that their unbelief is not from refusal of verbal acknowledgment and arrogance about obeying commands, accepting judgments, and persistence in verbal denial, up to other causes of unbelief, while having tasdiq of the heart, because it is not regarded with those indications, as in throwing the Quran into filth.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage defines tasdiq (assent) and addresses an objection. The author first distinguishes the logical term 'Kruwidan' (assent) from its linguistic meaning, citing Avicenna's al-Shifa. In logic, tasdiq is the mind's relating a judgment to reality with correspondence—not merely having the complete proposition in mind. It is explained as 'true-holding' (ṣādiq dāshtan), opposed to takdhib ('false-holding'). This definition repels the claim that judgment is a voluntary act (like positing or abstraction) and thus cannot be tasdiq or its part. The truth is that tasdiq is a kind of knowledge in the category of quality or passion; the soul merely acquiesces, accepts, and perceives the relation. Its attainment may be through voluntary acquisition or involuntarily. The commanded (in faith) must be acquired voluntarily. An objection arises: certainty without acquiescence (as in sophists) would be only conception (tasawwur), not tasdiq—which is false. The answer clarifies that logical tasdiq as defined by the logicians is different from the linguistic tasdiq used in faith. The scholars' agreement that linguistic tasdiq is what matters in faith is not undermined; it only requires additional conditions like choice. The objection about certainty without acquiescence is a separate discussion. However, the real issue is whether such certainty can substitute for acquiescence, and whether some unbelievers have certainty but not tasdiq—their unbelief stems from outward denial, not from lack of heart-tasdiq, which is disregarded due to contradictory signs (like throwing the Quran in filth).

Key Terms
إذعان
قبول
كسب
اختيار
كيف
انفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tasdiq is a voluntary action that the soul performs.
Correction: The author argues that tasdiq is a passive state (quality or passion) of the soul; it is not an act but an acquiescence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the true nature of tasdiq?
A) A voluntary act of positing or abstraction.
B) An act of the soul involving effort.
C) Acquiescence, acceptance, and perception of a relation.
D) A linguistic affirmation uttered by the tongue.

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq is a passive acquiescence of the soul, not an act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself lacking certainty in a core belief, do you attempt to force yourself to believe it anyway, or do you reflect on what means (kasb) you might employ to genuinely attain acquiescence—such as directed thought, study, or sensory evidence?
?
Consider a belief you hold deeply: was it acquired through voluntary effort (directed attention, reflection) or involuntarily (from upbringing or environment)? If it was involuntary, does this passage challenge you to seek a more intentional acquisition of certain truths?
?
The passage says that tasdiq is not an act but a passion—something that happens to the soul. Are you willing to admit that your most cherished convictions are not ultimately your own doing, but a gift or result of causes? How does that affect your humility before the truth?

Objection and Answer: Certainty Without Acquiescence
Author answers objection about certainty without acquiescence and clarifies the role of linguistic tasdiq in faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that certainty without acquiescence would be mere conception, and the author's response distinguishing logical tasdiq from linguistic tasdiq as used in faith.

Core Idea
Faith's tasdiq is linguistic, requiring choice and outward compliance, not just logical certainty.

The author now considers an objection: if certainty is obtained without acquiescence (as in sophists or some unbelievers), it would be only conception (tasawwur), not tasdiq, which is obviously false. The author responds by clarifying that his definition is for logical tasdiq, not the linguistic one used in faith. Faith's tasdiq is linguistic and requires conditions like choice and absence of denial. The objection about certainty without acquiescence is a separate issue; what matters is that unbelievers who have heart-tasdiq but show outward denial are still considered disbelievers due to contradictory signs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation to see the objection and the extended response.
2
Parse the objection
The objection states that certainty without acquiescence (as in sophists) would be conception only, not tasdiq. Understand why this is seen as problematic.
3
Identify the author's initial response
The author denies claiming that logical tasdiq is the same as linguistic; he distinguishes them. Note the phrase 'we do not claim except that logical tasdiq...'
4
Understand the conditions for faith
The author says that faith's tasdiq is linguistic and requires choice, absence of denial and arrogance. Also note the point about outward signs overriding heart-tasdiq.
Look for the example of throwing the Quran in filth.
5
Reflect on the separate discussion
The author notes that the issue of certainty vs. acquiescence is a separate discussion. He highlights the real concern: some unbelievers may have certainty but still be disbelievers due to outward refusal.

من أن «كرويدن» في المنطق غيره في اللغة. وقال في الشفاء : التصديق في قولك البياض عرض هو أن يحصل في الذهن نسبة صورة هذا التأليف إلى الأشياء أنفسها أنها مطابقة لها والتكذيب يخالف ذلك. فلم يجعل التصديق حصول النسبة التامة في الذهن على ما يفهمه البعض بل حصول أن ينسب الذهن الثبوت أو الانتفاء الذي بين طرفي التأليف إلى ما في نفس الأمر بالمطابقة . ومعناه نسبة الحكم إلى الصدق أعني صادق داشتن) وكرويدن وبينه بأنه ضد التكذيب الذي معناه النسبة إلى الكذب. أعني كاذب داشتن . وبهذا يندفع ما يقال إن الحكم فعل اختياري هو الإيقاع أو الانتزاع، فكيف يكون نفس التصديق أو جزءه . والتصديق قسم من العلم الذي هو من مقولة الكيف أو الانفعال ونعم ما قال من قال : الإسناد والإيقاع، ونحو ذلك، ألفاظ وعبارات والتحقيق أنه ليس للنفس ههنا تأثير وفعل. بل إذعان وقبول وإدراك أن النسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعة. نعم، حصول هذا التصديق قد يكون بالكسب أي مباشرة الأسباب بالاختيار كإلقاء الذهن وصرف النظر، وتوجيه الحواس وما أشبه ذلك. وقد يكون بدونه كمن وقع عليه الضوء فعلم أن الشمس طالعة . والمأمور به يجب أن يكون من الأول.

فإن قيل : فاليقين الحاصل بدون الإذعان والقبول، بل مع الجحود والاستكبار كما للسوفسطائي، ولبعض الكفار يكون من قبيل التصور دون التصديق . وهو ظاهر البطلان .

قلنا : نحن لا ندعي إلا كون التصديق المنطقي على ما يفسره رئيسهم، لا على ما يفهمه كل نساج وحلاج هو التصديق اللغوي، المقابل للتكذيب المعبر عنه «بكرويدن». وأنه لا يصح حينئذ إطلاق القول وإطباق القوم على أن المعتبر في الإيمان هو اللغوي، دون المنطقي. بل غايته أن يجب اشتراط أمور كالاختيار وترك الجحود والاستكبار. وأما أنه يلزم على قصد تقسيمه وتفسيره كون اليقين الخالي عن الإذعان والقبول تصوراً أو خارجاً عن التصور (۱)

(1) التصور حصول صورة الشيء في الذهن ، وقيل : هو إدراك الماهية من غير أن يحكم عليها بنفي أو إثبات .

?

Proof That Actions Are Not Part of Iman
Presentation of the Ash'ari position that actions are external to the reality of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six proofs presented by the Ash'ari theologian to establish that actions are external to the reality of iman (faith).

Core Idea
Iman is inner assent; actions are outward and separate.

This passage presents a concise argument from the Ash'ari school affirming that deeds are not part of the essential reality (haqiqa) of iman. The theologian cites linguistic, Qur'anic, and consensus-based proofs to distinguish between inner faith and outer works. Understanding these proofs clarifies a foundational point of Sunni orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to get an overview of the argument.
Notice the repeated reference to Qur'anic verses and the final consensus.
2
Identify each proof
The passage contains six distinct proofs. List them in order and note the evidence used for each: linguistic definition, Qur'anic commands, distinction between iman and deeds, fighting believers, and consensus.
The first proof is linguistic: iman means tasdiq and has not been transferred to include actions.
3
Reflect on the counterargument
Consider the common misunderstanding that commands to believers imply actions are part of iman. How do these proofs refute that view?
The commands address those who already have iman, so actions follow faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المقام الثالث . (إن الأعمال غير داخلة في حقيقة الإيمان لما ثبت أنه اسم للتصديق، ولا نقل وأنه لا ينفع عند معاينة العذاب ولاعمل ، وأن المؤمن قد يؤمر وينهي مثل : يا أيها الذين آمنوا كتب علكم الصيام ) (۱) و يا أيها الذين آمنوا لا تقدموا ) وللنصوص الدالة على أنهما أمران متغايران مثل : الذين آمنوا وعملوا الصالحات ) وقد يتفارفان مثل : ( وإن طائفتان من المؤمنين اقتتلوا (٢) . . الآية . وللإجماع على أن الإيمان شرط العبادة، وعلى أن من صدق وأقر فمات قبل أن يعمل فهو مؤمن.
He said: The third station. (Actions are not included in the reality of faith because it is established that it is a name for assent (tasdiq), and not transferred (naql), and that it does not benefit at the time of witnessing punishment, nor action, and that the believer may be commanded and prohibited, like: 'O you who have believed, upon you is prescribed fasting' and 'O you who have believed, do not precede', and for the texts indicating that they are two distinct things, like: 'Those who have believed and done righteous deeds', and they may separate, like: 'And if two groups of believers fight', and for the consensus that faith is a condition for worship, and that whoever believes and confesses and dies before acting is a believer.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is the author's argument (in the third station) that actions are not part of the reality (haqiqa) of iman. He provides several proofs: 1) Iman is lexically a name for tasdiq (assent) and has not been transferred (naql) to include actions. 2) Iman does not benefit when facing punishment (referring to the verse about Pharaoh's faith at drowning), and action alone does not avail. 3) The Qur'an addresses believers with commands and prohibitions (e.g., 'O you who have believed, fasting is prescribed for you'), implying they already have iman before acting. 4) The Qur'an often distinguishes between iman and good deeds (e.g., 'those who believe and do righteous deeds'), treating them as two separate entities. 5) The Qur'an shows believers fighting each other (i.e., 'if two groups of believers fight'), proving they remain believers despite sinful actions. 6) Consensus (ijma') that iman is a condition for worship, and that one who simply believes and confesses is a believer even if he dies before performing any actions.

Key Terms
إيمان
تصديق
عمل
نقل
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Qur'anic commands to believers (e.g., 'O you who have believed, fasting is prescribed for you') prove that actions are part of iman.
Correction: These commands address an already existing iman; they do not define iman itself. The believer is commanded to act because of his iman, not to acquire iman.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the proofs presented in this passage that actions are not part of iman?
A) The linguistic meaning of iman is tasdiq, and it has not been transferred.
B) The believers are commanded and prohibited, showing their iman precedes action.
C) The verse 'if two groups of believers fight' shows sinful actions do not negate iman.
D) The Prophet said that actions are the essence of faith.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school maintains that iman is purely tasdiq (assent) and does not include actions, based on linguistic, textual, and consensus evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged the strength of your own or others' faith based on outward actions? How does the clear separation between iman and actions in this passage confront that tendency? What would it mean for you to trust Allah's acceptance based on inner assent rather than performance?
?
The passage cites the verse about believers fighting each other. Is there a person in your life you have considered 'less of a believer' due to their sins? How can you reconcile your judgment with the fact that Allah calls them 'believers' despite their actions?
?
If iman is purely inner assent, and actions are separate, does that make you complacent about obedience? Where is the line between trusting in Allah's mercy and taking His commands lightly? Ask yourself: Does your heart truly assent to what Allah has revealed, or are you relying on your deeds to feel secure?

Definition from al-Kifayah: Inseparability of Islam and Iman
Author presents another definition from al-Kifayah, proving Islam and Iman cannot be separated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Iman and Islam from al-Kifayah and why they are considered inseparable in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Iman and Islam are two sides of the same coin, inseparable in their ruling.

This short passage from al-Kifayah offers a crisp definition of Iman and Islam, emphasizing their conceptual and legal unity. While the terms may seem distinct, the author argues that they cannot be separated in practice or divine judgment. Understanding this point is key to grasping early theological debates on faith and submission.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Begin by reading the Arabic text slowly. Notice the key terms: تصديق, انقياد, حكم.
The passage is concise but packs a lot of meaning.
2
Study the definitions
Identify how Iman and Islam are defined: Iman as 'affirming God as true' regarding commands and prohibitions, Islam as 'submission and humility' before God's divinity.
3
Analyze the logical link
The passage states that submission is not realized without accepting command and prohibition. How does this connect Iman and Islam?
Iman involves affirming the commands, which inherently implies submission to them.
4
Understand the ruling
The conclusion: Iman and Islam are not separated in ruling (ḥukman). This means they are legally equivalent and one cannot exist without the other.
This is a key theological claim against those who might separate them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في الكفاية : الإيمان هو تصديق الله فيما أخبر من أوامره ونواهيه والإسلام هو الانقياد والخضوع لألوهيته. وذا لا يتحقق إلا بقبول الأمر والنهي . فالإيمان لا ينفك عن الإسلام حكماً، فلا يتغايران.
And it is said in al-Kifayah: Faith is affirming God as true in what He has informed of His commands and prohibitions, and Islam is submission and humility before His divinity. And this is not realized except by accepting the command and prohibition. So faith is not separated from Islam in terms of ruling, so they do not differ.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents a definition from the work al-Kifayah. It defines Īmān (faith) as taṣdīq (affirmation/assent) to God regarding His commands and prohibitions, and Islām as al-inqiyād (submission) and al-khuḍūʿ (humility) to His divinity. The author then notes that this submission is not actualized except by accepting the command and prohibition. Therefore, Īmān cannot be separated from Islām in terms of legal ruling (ḥukman), meaning that wherever Īmān is present, Islām is necessarily present, and vice versa. Thus the two are not different (lā yataghāyarān). This argument builds on the conceptual linkage: if Īmān is affirmation of God's commands, then submission (Islām) to those commands is inherent. The passage is very concise but makes a strong point: the two are not distinct in legal effect, even if their definitions differ verbally.

Key Terms
التصديق
الانقياد
الحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that Iman and Islam are different in meaning and can exist separately.
Correction: Al-Kifayah argues that they are inseparable in ruling; Iman necessarily entails Islam, and vice versa.

Checkpoint
According to al-Kifayah, what is the relationship between Iman and Islam?
A) Iman is more specific.
B) Islam is more specific.
C) They are inseparable in ruling.
D) They are completely distinct.

Key Takeaway
Iman and Islam are legally inseparable: affirming God's commands (Iman) inherently requires submission (Islam), and both carry the same ruling.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life do you affirm God's commands with your tongue but resist submitting to them with your actions? What would it take to close that gap today?
?
This passage says submission is not realized except by accepting the command and prohibition. Is there a clear command of God that you have not fully accepted? Why, and what is the cost of that resistance to your faith?
?
If Iman and Islam are inseparable in ruling, then your claim to faith is judged by your submission. Will you let this truth expose the distance between what you say you believe and how you live—and then ask God for the strength to change?

The Debate on Whether Faith Increases and Decreases
Debate on faith increase with proofs and positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical debate on whether faith (iman) can increase and decrease, and how it hinges on the definition of iman as either tasdiq (assent) or works.

Core Idea
Whether faith increases depends entirely on what you think faith is.

This passage presents a foundational debate in Islamic theology: does faith increase and decrease? At stake is whether salvation can fluctuate. The discussion reveals that there is no simple answer; it depends on whether we define iman as inner conviction or as including works. As you read, notice how each side uses the same Qur'anic verses to support opposite conclusions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the shift from the initial premise to the proof and then the response.
2
Identify the two main positions
Notice that the passage first presents the view that faith increases (from texts and reason) and then the response that reinterprets that increase. Then it explicitly states the two schools: the Ash'aris/Mu'tazilis (increase) and the Hanafis (no increase).
The response does not flatly deny the texts but redefines what 'increase' means.
3
Understand the role of definition
Focus on the final statement: the whole disagreement is a branch of the interpretation of iman. If iman is tasdiq, it does not vary; if it is works, it does. This is the key insight.
4
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: How does this debate affect one's view of salvation and religious practice? If faith can decrease, what does that mean for a believer's security?
This connects to broader theological concerns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اليقين، وهو لا يتفاوت ، وإنما يتفاوت إذا جعل اسماً للطاعة، ولهذا قيل : الخلاف مبني على الخلاف في تفسير الإيمان، لكنه إنما يصح إذا لم يجعل ترك العمل خروجاً عن الإيمان، وحينئذ يكون التفاوت في كمال الإيمان، لا في أصله . وأجيب بعد تسليم أن التصديق هو اليقين، وأن اليقين هو المعتبر في حق الكل يمنع قبوله التفاوت كما في اليقين الضروري والنظري، بعد زوال التردد والخفاء . تمسك القائلون بالتفاوت بأن إيمان آحاد الأمة لا يساوي إيمان الأنبياء قطعاً، و بالنصوص الصريحة في ذلك :
وإذا تليت عليهم آياته زادتهم إيماناً ) (1) ليزدادوا إيماناً مع إيمانهم (٢) ویزداد الذين آمنوا إيماناً) (۳)
وفي الحديث : « إن الإيمان يزيد حتى يدخل صاحبه الجنة ) .
وأجيب بأن المراد الزيادة بحسب الدوام والثبات والأعداد، أو بحسب زيادة ما يجب الإيمان به عند ملاحظة التفاصيل، أو المراد زيادة ثمراته وأنواره . )
وهو مذهب الأشاعرة والمعتزلة، والمحكى عن الشافعي ( رحمه الله) وكثير من العلماء أن الإيمان يزيد وينقص . وعند أبي حنيفة (رحمه الله) وأصحابه وكثير من العلماء - وهو اختيار إمام الحرمين - أنه لا يزيد ولا ينقص ، لأنه اسم للتصديق البالغ حد الجزم والإذعان ولا يتصور فيه الزيادة والنقصان.والمصدق إذا ضم الطاعات إليه أو ارتكب المعاصي، فتصديقه بحالة لم يتغير أصلاً ، وإنما يتفاوت إذا كان اسماً للطاعات المتفاوتة قلة وكثرة . ولهذا قال الإمام الرازي وغيره : إن هذا الخلاف فرع تفسير الإيمان .
فإن قلنا هو التصديق، فلا يتفاوت وإن قلنا هو الأعمال فمتفاوت .
Certainty, and it does not vary. But it varies if it is made a name for obedience. For this reason it was said: the disagreement is based on the disagreement in the interpretation of faith (iman). But this is only valid if abandoning action is not made an exit from faith; then the variation is in the perfection of faith, not in its essence. It was answered, after conceding that tasdiq (assent) is certainty, and that certainty is what is considered with respect to all, that it prevents it from admitting variation, as in necessary and theoretical certainty after the removal of hesitation and hiddenness. Those who affirm variation held by [arguing that] the faith of ordinary members of the community is certainly not equal to the faith of the prophets, and by clear texts to that effect: "And when His verses are recited to them, they increase them in faith" (Quran 8:2); "That they may increase in faith upon their faith" (Quran 48:4); "And He will increase those who believe in faith" (Quran 74:31). And in the hadith: "Indeed faith increases until it brings its possessor into Paradise." It was answered that what is meant by increase is in terms of continuity, steadfastness, and numbers, or in terms of the increase of what must be believed in when observing details, or what is meant is the increase of its fruits and lights. This is the doctrine of the Ash'aris and Mu'tazilis, and it is related from al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) and many scholars that faith increases and decreases. According to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) and his companions and many scholars—and it is the choice of Imam al-Haramayn—that it does not increase or decrease, because it is a name for tasdiq that reaches the level of certainty and submission (judhām and idh'ān) and increase and decrease are inconceivable in it. And the one who affirms, if he performs acts of obedience or commits sins, his tasdiq remains in its state, unchanged at all; rather it varies if it is a name for acts of obedience that vary in fewness and multitude. For this reason Imam al-Razi and others said: this disagreement is a branch of the interpretation of faith. For if we say it is tasdiq, then it does not vary; and if we say it is works, then it varies.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage presents the classical debate about whether faith (iman) can increase and decrease. It begins by noting that certainty (yaqin) itself does not vary, but if iman is defined as obedience, then variation is possible. The disagreement thus stems from the definition of iman. The author then presents the proof from those who affirm variation: the faith of ordinary Muslims is not equal to that of prophets, and there are explicit Quranic verses and a hadith indicating increase. The response is that these texts refer to increase in constancy, in the number of beliefs when detailed, or in the fruits and lights of faith, not in the essence of faith itself. The passage then states the two main positions: the Ash'aris and Mu'tazilis (and many scholars including al-Shafi'i) hold that faith increases and decreases; the Hanafis (including Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Haramayn) hold that it does not, because faith is tasdiq (assent) of a certain level, which does not admit variation. If one performs good or bad deeds, his tasdiq remains unchanged. The variation only occurs if iman is defined as works. Therefore, as al-Razi says, the whole disagreement is a branch of the interpretation of iman.

تصديق
يقين
زيادة
نقصان

طاعة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that increase in faith always refers to increase in the essence (asl) of faith.
Correction: The passage clarifies that increase can refer to its perfection or fruits, not necessarily its essence. Those who deny increase still affirm that the fruits of faith increase.

Checkpoint

B) The interpretation of faith (iman) itself

Key Takeaway
The disagreement over increase/decrease of faith is fundamentally a disagreement about the definition of iman itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If iman is defined as certainty of the heart (tasdiq), then your sins do not decrease your iman in essence, only its perfection. Does this truth make you more grateful for the mercy of Allah, or does it tempt you to neglect obedience? Which reaction is more honest about your current state of faith? This week, will you focus on deepening your certainty or on increasing your outward obedience—and how will you ensure both are sincere?
?
The passage reveals that the debate on increase/decrease is rooted in how you define iman. How do you personally define iman? Do you equate it with inner conviction alone, or do you insist that works are part of it? Does your definition match how you live? When you sin, do you feel your faith has decreased, or do you see it as a lapse in perfection? Let this lesson force you to examine the gap between your theology and your lived experience.
?
The Quranic verses about increase in faith are clear in their wording. The Hanafis reinterpret them to avoid implying variation in tasdiq. When you read such verses, do you feel your faith increasing? If yes, what is increasing—your certainty, your actions, or both? If no, does that worry you? This lesson demands that you decide: is your faith something that can grow, and if so, what are you doing to make it grow? Do not settle for a comfortable answer.

Resolving the Ta'wil-Takfir Problem
Resolving the ta'wil problem by distinguishing certain texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the issue of ta'wil in usul al-din is resolved by distinguishing texts known with certainty from those that are not, and why this distinction prevents indiscriminate takfir.

Core Idea
Not every ta'wil leads to takfir; only interpretation of texts known with certainty as literal does.

In this passage, the author tackles a practical problem: if we declare takfir on anyone who interprets foundational texts, we would condemn many Muslim groups, but if we never do, we risk not condemning clear deniers. The resolution lies in distinguishing between texts that are decisively literal and those that are open to interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
Consider the two horns: either all mu'awwils are deniers (too harsh) or none are (too lenient). Notice why each horn leads to an unacceptable consequence.
The first horn would make takfir of many Islamic sects necessary; the second would forbid takfir of those who deny bodily resurrection, etc.
2
Identify the resolution
Find the key distinction the author introduces: texts known with certainty (qat'an) from the religion to be taken literally cannot be interpreted; doing so is takdhib.
This limits takfir to only those who interpret such decisive texts.
3
Apply the distinction
Reflect on the examples: denial of bodily resurrection, temporal creation, God's knowledge of particulars. Their interpretations are not more far-fetched than those of ahl al-haqq, but the decisive texts make the difference.
This distinction keeps takfir from being applied indiscriminately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا يندفع إشكال آخر، وهو أن صاحب التأويل في الأصول إما أن يجعل من المكذبين ، فيلزم تكفير كثير من الفرق الإسلامية كأهل البدع والأهواء . بل المختلفين من أهل الحق وإما أن لا يجعل فيلزم عدم تكفير المنكرين لحشر الأجساد ، وحدوث العالم وعلم الباري بالجزئيات (۲) فإن تأويلاتهم ليست بأبعد من تأويلات أهل الحق للنصوص الظاهرة في خلاف مذهبهم وذلك لأن من النصوص ما علم قطعاً من الدين أنه على ظاهره، فتأويله تكذيب للنبي، بخلاف البعض .
And by this another problem is repelled, namely that the one who engages in interpretation (ta'wil) in the fundamentals is either made among the deniers, leading to the takfir of many Islamic sects like the people of innovation and desires, indeed the disputants among the people of truth; or he is not made [among them], leading to the non-takfir of the deniers of the resurrection of bodies, the temporal creation of the world, and the knowledge of the Creator of particulars, for their interpretations are not more far-fetched than the interpretations of the people of truth of the apparent texts contrary to their school, because among the texts are those known with certainty from the religion to be taken literally, so their interpretation is a denial of the Prophet, contrary to some.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage resolves a problem arising from the previous discussion: the status of the mu'awwil (one who interprets) in usul al-din. If we consider every mu'awwil a mukadhdhib (denier), we would be forced to declare takfir upon many Islamic groups, including people of innovation (ahl al-bida') and desires (ahwa'), and even those who differ among ahl al-haqq (the people of truth). If we do not consider them deniers, then we would not declare takfir upon those who deny the bodily resurrection, the temporal creation of the world, and God's knowledge of particulars—despite their interpretation being no more far-fetched than the ta'wil of ahl al-haqq when they interpret apparent texts that contradict their school. The resolution is that among the texts, there are some that are known with certainty (qat'an) from the religion to be taken literally (zahir). Their ta'wil constitutes takdhib of the Prophet, unlike other texts that are not decisively literal. Thus, the distinction lies in the degree of certainty; only ta'wil of decisive texts warrants takfir.

Key Terms
تأويل
أصول
مكذبين
تكفير
قطع
ظاهر
نص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All ta'wil in fundamental matters leads to takfir.
Correction: Only ta'wil of texts known with certainty from the religion to be literal constitutes denial and thus leads to takfir. Other interpretations are permissible without takfir.

Checkpoint
How does the author resolve the problem of ta'wil in usul regarding takfir?
A) All mu'awwils are considered deniers and thus disbelievers.
B) No mu'awwil is considered a denier, so no one is declared disbeliever.
C) The distinction depends on whether the interpreted text is known with certainty from the religion to be literal.
D) The distinction depends on the intention of the mu'awwil.

Key Takeaway
The decisive factor for takfir is whether the interpreted text is known with certainty from the religion to be literal; only then is ta'wil considered denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time you disagreed with a fellow Muslim on a matter of doctrine. Did you assume their interpretation was a form of denial? How does this passage's distinction between decisive and non-decisive texts change how you view that disagreement? Commit to revisiting one such disagreement with a more discerning heart.
?
There is a tendency to label those we disagree with as innovators or misguided. Are there any groups or individuals you need to reconsider your judgment of, because the texts they interpret may not be among those known with certainty? Resolve to learn more about their actual basis before judging.
?
Honestly, which of your own beliefs are built on texts known with certainty from the religion, and which are based on personal reasoning or weaker evidence? Are you willing to be corrected if one of your cherished interpretations is not based on a decisive text? Take a moment to identify one such belief and seek clarity.

Refining the Definition of Kufr: The Subject of Takdhib
Clarifying the subject of takdhib: the mukallaf and the sabi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the definition of kufr as takdhib is refined by specifying its subject as the mukallaf, and how this affects the status of the intelligent child.

Core Idea
Kufr is defined only in relation to the legally responsible person.

In this lesson, we examine a critical refinement to the definition of kufr as takdhib. The author clarifies that this definition applies specifically to the mukallaf, thereby excluding the intelligent child who has not yet reached legal responsibility. This refinement ensures that the definition is precise and accounts for different scholarly views on the child's faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the original passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb the author's own wording. Then read the literal translation to ensure understanding.
Notice that the passage uses two conditional scenarios.
2
Identify the refinement: the subject is the mukallaf
The passage starts by making explicit that the intended meaning of takdhib or non-belief is from the mukallaf. This exclusion is the first refinement.
The term mukallaf is crucial in Islamic law—it means one who is legally responsible for religious duties.
3
Understand the nuance regarding the intelligent child
The passage then discusses a second scenario: for scholars who hold that the child's faith is valid, the definition is adjusted accordingly. Consider why this nuance matters for the definition of kufr.
This shows that definitions in theology can be sensitive to different legal premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لا يخفى أن المراد التكذيب، أو عدم التصديق من المكلف ، ليخرج الصبي العاقل الذي لم يصدق أو صرح بالتكذيب. وأما عند القائلين بصحة إيمانه، وبأنه يكفر بصريح التكذيب وإن لم يكفر بترك التصديق، فالمراد التكذيب ممن يصح الإيمان وعدم التصديق ممن يجب عليه الإيمان ...
Then it is not hidden that what is meant is denial (takdhib) or non-belief from the morally responsible person (mukallaf), to exclude the intelligent child (sabi 'aqil) who has not believed or explicitly uttered denial. As for those who hold the validity of his faith and that he becomes a disbeliever by explicit denial though not by leaving belief, then what is meant is denial from one whose faith is valid and non-belief from one upon whom faith is obligatory.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage refines the definition of kufr as takdhib by specifying the subject. It clarifies that the intended meaning of takdhib or 'adam al-tasdiq (non-belief) is from the mukallaf (the legally responsible person). This excludes the sabi 'aqil (intelligent child) who has not yet believed or who explicitly denies—such a child is not considered a disbeliever for lacking belief according to the definition, because he is not yet obligated. The author then notes a nuance for those scholars who hold that the sabi's faith is valid, and that he becomes a disbeliever only by explicit denial (not by mere lack of belief). In that view, the definition's 'takdhib' means denial from one whose faith is valid (i.e., the sabi), and 'non-belief' means from one upon whom iman is obligatory (the mukallaf). Thus, the definition is tailored to the context of legal responsibility.

تصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Anyone who does not believe is a disbeliever.
Correction: The passage clarifies that kufr is defined from the mukallaf, so the intelligent child who has not believed or explicitly denied is not considered a disbeliever.

Checkpoint

C) The one who denies out of ignorance.
D) The one who believes but commits sins.

Key Takeaway
The definition of kufr as takdhib applies strictly to the mukallaf, thereby excluding the intelligent child who is not yet legally responsible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The intelligent child is excused for not believing because he is not yet obligated. But you are obligated. What does that mean for your own hesitation or doubt? Are you content with merely not denying, or do you actively affirm faith in your heart?
?
The passage refines the definition of kufr to apply only to the mukallaf. If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow, would He find you among those who truly believed as required, or among those who neglected their responsibility?

Al-Qadi's Definition of Kufr as Jahd and Its Defense
Al-Qadi's definition, objection, and defense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Qadi's definition of kufr as denial, the objections raised against it, and how it is defended by restricting denial to matters known with certainty.

Core Idea
Kufr is denial, but only of matters known with certainty from religion.

Al-Qadi's definition of kufr as jahd (denial) is both intuitive and controversial. While it captures the essence of disbelief, critics argue it is too broad or too narrow. In this passage, we see the definition, the objections, and the thoughtful response that refines it to matters of certain knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Pay attention to the flow: definition, objection, answer.
2
Identify the definition and objection
Find al-Qadi's definition and the two points of the objection: non-convertibility and over-inclusion.
3
Understand the answer's restriction
The answer restricts 'jahd' to matters known with certainty (qat'an). See how this resolves both objection points.
4
Compare with takdhib definition
Reflect on why this definition might be superior to defining kufr as denial of the Prophet.
The passage explicitly mentions the kufr of Iblis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال القاضي : الكفر هو الجحد بالله ، وربما يفسر الجحد بالجهل. واعترض بعدم انعكاسه فإن كثيراً من الكفرة عارفون بالله تعالی، مصدقون به (۱) غیر جاحدين. وإداريد الجحد أو الجهل أعم من أن يكون بوجوده أو وحدانيته، أو شيء من صفاته وأفعاله وأحكامه، لزم تكفير كثير من أهل الإسلام المخالفين في الأصول لأن الحق واحد وفاقاً. وأجيب بأن المراد الجحد به في شيء مما علم قطعاً أنه من أحكامه أو الجهل بذلك إجمالاً وتفصيلاً، وحينئذ يطرد وينعكس . بل ربما يكون أحسن من التعريف بتكذيب النبي عليه السلام) أو عدم تصديقه . لشموله الكفر بالله من غير توسط النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ككفر إبليس .
And al-Qadi said: Kufr is denial (jahd) with Allah, and sometimes jahd is interpreted as ignorance. And it was objected that it is not convertible, for many disbelievers know Allah, believe in Him, and are not deniers. And if denial or ignorance is more general than being in His existence, His oneness, or something of His attributes, actions, or judgments, then it would necessitate the takfir of many Muslims who differ in fundamentals, because the truth is one by agreement. And it was answered that what is meant is denial with respect to something known with certainty to be among His judgments, or ignorance of that in summary and detail, and then it is comprehensive and convertible. Indeed, perhaps it is better than the definition by denial of the Prophet or non-belief in him, because it includes kufr with Allah without the intermediary of the Prophet, like the kufr of Iblis.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents al-Qadi's definition of kufr as al-jahd bi-Allah (denial with Allah), sometimes interpreted as jahl (ignorance). An objection is raised: the definition is not convertible (in'ikas) because many disbelievers know Allah and believe in Him—they are not deniers. The objection also notes that if jahd or jahl is taken broadly (existence, oneness, attributes, actions, judgments), it would wrongly include many Muslims who differ in usul, since the truth is one. The answer is that the intended meaning is jahd concerning something known with certainty (qat'an) to be among His judgments, or ignorance of that in summary or detail. Thus defined, the definition is both comprehensive (mutarid) and convertible (mun'akis). The author suggests this definition may be better than the takdhib one because it covers kufr with Allah without the intermediary of the Prophet, such as the kufr of Iblis, who denied directly.

Key Terms
جحد
جهل
كفر بالله
قطع
انعكاس
إبليس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Qadi's definition of kufr as jahd is too broad and would condemn many Muslims.
Correction: The definition is restricted to denial of matters known with certainty from religion, which excludes differences in interpretation.

Checkpoint
How does the defender of al-Qadi's definition restrict the term 'jahd' to avoid the objection of over-inclusion?
A) By limiting it to denial of God's existence alone.
B) By specifying it is denial concerning something known with certainty from religion.
C) By requiring explicit verbal denial.
D) By including only those who disbelieve in the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Al-Qadi's definition of kufr as denial, when restricted to matters of certain knowledge, is both comprehensive and convertible, even covering the kufr of Iblis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself acknowledging Allah's existence and even His attributes, yet living as if His commands are optional? Examine your daily choices—are there any areas where you quietly deny a clear obligation because it is difficult? What can you change starting today to treat Allah's certain commands as non-negotiable?
?
The objection in this passage claims that disbelievers 'know Allah, believe in Him, and are not deniers.' Is your knowledge of Allah and belief in Him merely intellectual? Or does it translate into submission? What false belief are you still holding onto that contradicts a matter you know is certain from religion? Repent and act on it now.
?
Al-Qadi's definition excludes minor disagreements among Muslims. Examine your heart: do you ever label fellow believers who differ on non-essential matters as 'not true Muslims'? Are you using takfir loosely? How can you guard your tongue and heart against unjust takfir, while still defending the certain truths of Islam?

Definition of Fasiq and Mubtadi' and the Ruling on Istihlal
The author defines fasiq and mubtadi' and states that deeming sin permissible is kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of fasiq and mubtadi', and why deeming sin permissible is an act of disbelief.

Core Idea
Deeming a sin permissible is not just sin—it is unbelief.

This passage from the Maqasid clarifies key terms in Islamic theology: fasiq (sinner) and mubtadi' (innovator). More importantly, it distinguishes between merely committing a sin and deeming it permissible—the latter crossing into kufr. Understanding these distinctions is critical for correctly assessing people's religious status.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style of the matn.
2
Identify the definition of fisq
Look for the definition of fisq (sin) and note the two ways one becomes a fasiq: committing a major sin or persisting in a minor sin. Also note the exception for those with a valid ta'wil (interpretation).
The term 'baghi' (rebel) is excluded because they act on interpretation.
3
Recognize the ruling on istihlal
Find the statement that deeming a definitively prohibited act permissible (istihlal) or treating it lightly (istihana) is kufr, not merely fisq.
This is a crucial boundary: intention matters.
4
Understand the definition of mubtadi'
Read the definition of mubtadi' as one who opposes the creed of Ahl al-Haqq. Note that his ruling is like that of the fasiq.
Innovation in creed is treated similarly to sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثامن) - حكم المؤمن والكافر والفاسق ما مر، والفسق هو الخروج عن طاعة الله بارتكاب الكبيرة، أو الإصرار على الصغيرة وقد يقيد بعدم التأويل احترازاً عن الباغي. وأما استحلال ما هو معصية قطعاً والاستهانة به فكفر. والمبتدع هو من خالف في العقيدة طريقة أهل الحق . وهو كالفاسق .
Eighth Section: The ruling of the believer, the disbeliever, and the sinner has passed. Fisq (sin) is departing from obedience to Allah by committing a major sin (kabīra), or persisting in a minor sin (ṣaghīra), and it may be qualified by the absence of interpretation (ta’wīl) to exclude the rebel (bāghī). As for deeming permissible (istiḥlāl) what is definitely disobedience and treating it lightly (istihāna), that is kufr (disbelief). The innovator (mubtadiʿ) is one who opposes in creed (ʿaqīda) the way of the people of truth (ṭarīqat ahl al-ḥaqq). He is like the sinner (fāsiq).
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage defines two important terms: fasiq (sinner) and mubtadi' (innovator), and states a key principle regarding istihlal (deeming sin permissible). The passage begins by stating that the ruling of believers, disbelievers, and sinners has already been mentioned (in previous sections). Then it defines fisq (sin) as departing from obedience to Allah by committing a major sin (kabira) or persisting (israr) in a minor sin (saghira). It adds that this definition is qualified by the absence of ta'wil (interpretation) in order to exclude the baghi (rebel), meaning one who rebels against a just ruler based on his own interpretation is not considered a fasiq. Then it states that istihlal (deeming permissible) of what is definitively a sin, as well as istihana (treating it lightly), is kufr (disbelief), not merely fisq. Finally, it defines mubtadi' as one who opposes in 'aqida (creed) the way of ahl al-haqq (the people of truth, i.e., Ahl al-Sunna). The ruling of the mubtadi' is like that of the fasiq. This establishes that innovations in creed are treated similarly to major sins in terms of religious status.

Key Terms
فسق (fisq)
كبيرة (kabira)
صغيرة (saghira)
الإصرار (israr)
الباغي (baghi)
التأويل (ta'wil)
استحلال (istihlal)
استهانة (istihana)
كفر (kufr)
مبتدع (mubtadi')
طريقة أهل الحق (tariqat ahl al-haqq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that istihlal (deeming sin permissible) is just a major sin, not disbelief.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that istihlal of something definitively prohibited is kufr, not just fisq. Treating sin lightly (istihana) is also kufr.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is considered kufr (disbelief)?
A) Committing a major sin
B) Persisting in a minor sin
C) Deeming a definitively prohibited act permissible
D) Opposing the creed of the people of truth

Key Takeaway
Deeming a sin permissible (istihlal) is an act of disbelief, not merely sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a sin you have been treating as small or insignificant. The passage says persistence on minor sin is fisq and deeming it permissible is kufr. Is there a 'small' sin you have been persisting in without a valid reason? What step will you take today to stop and repent sincerely?
?
Have you ever justified a sin by telling yourself that Allah is forgiving or that you intend to repent later? This lesson warns that istihlal—deeming a sin permissible—is disbelief. Are you treating any sin as permissible in your heart? How will you change that attitude right now?
?
The innovator is like a sinner. Are there any beliefs or practices you hold that oppose the way of the people of truth (Ahl al-Sunna)? How can you learn the correct creed and abandon innovations, even if they feel comfortable?

Defining Imama: Why It Belongs to Kalam
Defines imama and explains its inclusion in kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of imama as general leadership and the historical reason why its study was included in kalam rather than remaining solely in fiqh.

Core Idea
Imama is a fiqh topic studied in kalam because heretical beliefs made it a theological necessity.

This passage introduces the topic of imama (leadership) and clarifies its nature. While imama logically belongs to fiqh as a communal obligation, the author explains why kalam scholars also address it. Understanding this dual placement helps you see how theology interacts with practical religious law.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's own words introduce you to the topic.
Notice the precise wording of the definition.
2
Analyze the definition
Identify the key components: imama is a general leadership (رياسة عامة) in religion and worldly life, as a caliphate from the Prophet.
The term 'خلافة' links it to succession.
3
Find the justification for inclusion in kalam
Look for the reason why imama is discussed in kalam: because of corrupt beliefs (اعتقادات فاسدة) spread by heretics.
This shows the defensive role of kalam.
4
Understand the original home of imama
Note the author's statement that there is no dispute that imama belongs to fiqh. It is a communal obligation (فرض كفاية).
This reaffirms its practical nature.
5
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Consider how a fiqh topic becomes part of kalam due to historical circumstances. This illustrates the interdisciplinary nature of Islamic sciences.
Think of other topics that cross boundaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: الفصل الرابع - في الإمامة. (وهي رياسة عامة في أمر الدين والدنيا خلافة عن النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) وأحكامه في الفروع. إلا أنه لما شاعت من أهل البدع اعتقادات فاسدة مخلة بكثير من القواعد، أدرجت مباحثها في الكلام). لا نزاع في أن مباحث الإمامة بعلم الفروع أليق لرجوعها إلى أن القيام بالإمامة ونصب الإمام الموصوف بالصفات المخصوصة من فروض الكفايات.
He said: The Fourth Chapter – On Imama. (It is a general leadership in matters of religion and worldly life, as a caliphate from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his rulings in secondary matters. However, because corrupt beliefs harmful to many principles spread among the people of innovation, its discussions were included in kalam.) There is no dispute that the discussions of imama are more appropriate to the science of secondary matters (fiqh), because establishing the imama and appointing the imam described with specific qualities is among communal obligations (fard kifaya).
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Imama. It first defines imama as a general leadership in religious and worldly affairs, as a succession to the Prophet. Then it explains why imama is studied in kalam: because heretical groups introduced false beliefs about it that undermine many principles of religion. Otherwise, it would naturally belong to fiqh (the science of practical rulings). The author then notes that there is no disagreement that the topics of imama are more fitting to fiqh, since establishing an imam with the required qualities is a communal obligation. This acknowledgment shows the methodological justification for including imama in the theological curriculum.

خلافة
فروض الكفايات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think imama is purely a theological concept with no connection to practical law.
Correction: The author clarifies that imama is primarily a fiqh topic (communal obligation) but included in kalam due to heretical distortions.

Checkpoint

C) Because it is a communal obligation.
D) Because it is a branch of eschatology.

Key Takeaway
Imama belongs to fiqh but is studied in kalam to counteract heretical distortions.

Why Imamate Is Included in Kalam: Definition and Conditions
Taftazani explains why imamate is in kalam and gives definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the topic of imamate was incorporated into the science of kalam, how it is defined, and the key discussions about its conditions, especially the condition of unity (waḥda).

Core Idea
Imamate is a core topic in kalam because of historical corrupt beliefs, and its definition requires careful conditions.

This passage from Taftazani's Sharh al-Maqasid explains the historical and theological reasons for including imamate in kalam. He begins by noting the spread of corrupt beliefs from groups like the Rawafid and Khawarij, which threatened Islamic foundations and the reputation of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Consequently, the mutakallimun attached this subject to kalam, even incorporating it into the very definition of the science. The passage then presents definitions of imamate and engages with objections regarding the condition of unity and the nature of vicegerency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation to get an overall sense of the argument. Notice the flow from reason for inclusion to definition to objections.
The passage is dense; reading twice helps.
2
Identify the reason for inclusion
Look for the phrase 'لما شاعت... اعتقادات فاسدة' and understand why the mutakallimun felt compelled to include imamate in kalam.
The key is the spread of corrupt beliefs from Rawafid and Khawarij.
3
Understand the definition of imamate
The definition is 'رياسة عامة في أمر الدين والدنيا، خلافة عن النبي'. Note how it excludes prophethood and partial leaderships.
Pay attention to the two restrictions: 'عامة' and 'خلافة'.
4
Examine the debate on unity
Al-Razi's definition adds 'لشخص من الأشخاص' which implies unity. The objection is that unity is a condition, not a constitutive element. The author argues it is more like a constitutive element.
Understand the difference between condition (shart) and constitutive element (muqawwim).
5
Consider the vicegerency objection
An objector says vicegerency only applies to direct appointment. The response is that istikhlaf can be indirect too.
This clarifies that the definition covers both direct and indirect succession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا، ولكن لما شاعت بين الناس في باب الإمامة اعتقادات فاسدة واختلافات بل اختلافات باردة سيما من فرق الروافض والخوارج ومالت كل فئة إلى تعصبات تكاد تفضي إلى رفض كثير من قواعد الإسلام، ونقض عقائد المسلمين والقدح في الخلفاء الراشدين، مع القطع بأنه ليس للبحث عن أحوالهم، واستحقاقهم وأفضليتهم كثير تعلق بأفعال المكلفين ألحق المتكلمون هذا الباب بأبواب الكلام ، وربما أدرجوه في تعريفه حيث قالوا : هو العلم الباحث عن أصول الصانع والنبوه والإمامة والمعاد، وما يتصل بذلك على قانون الإسلام والإمامة رئاسة عامة في أمر الدين والدنيا ، خلافة عن النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) وبهذا القيد خرجت النبوة، وبقيد العموم مثل القضاء والرياسة في بعض النواحي، وكذا رئاسة من جعلة الإمام نائباً عنه على الإطلاق، فإنها لا تعم الإمامة.
وقال الإمام الرازي (۱) : هي رياسة عامة في الدين والدنيا، لشخص من الأشخاص، وقال : هو احتراز عن كل الأمة إذا عزلوا الإمام لفسقه . وكأنه أراد بكل الأمة أهل الحل والعقد، واعتبر رياستهم على من عداهم أو على كل من آحاد الأمة. ومع هذا يرد ، عليه أن الوحدة من شرائط الإمامة لا من مقوماتها. وفي الشروط كثرة وعلى اشتراطها أدلة ويمكن أن يقال: إنها بالمقومات أشبه من جهة أنه لا يقال لجميع الأمة حينئذ أئمة . بخلاف الإمام الجاهل أو الفاسق أو نحو ذلك، وعلى هذا ينبغي أن لا يقال لشخصين بايعهما الأمة أنهما إمامان .
فإن قيل : الخلافة عن النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) إنما تكون فيمن استخلفه النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) . ولا يصدق التعريف على إمامة البيعة (۲) ونحوها ، فضلاً عن رئاسة النائب العام للإمام . قلنا : لو سلم فالاستخلاف أعم من أن يكون بوسط أو بدونه .
This. But when corrupt beliefs and differences, indeed cold differences, spread among people concerning the topic of imamate, especially from the groups of the Rawāfiḍ and Khawārij, and each faction inclined toward fanaticisms that almost lead to the rejection of many foundations of Islam, the nullification of the beliefs of Muslims, and slander against the Rightly Guided Caliphs—while being certain that inquiry into their conditions, worthiness, and superiority has little connection to the actions of the obligated—the mutakallimūn attached this topic to the topics of kalām. And perhaps they included it in its definition when they said: 'It is the science that investigates the principles of the Maker, prophethood, imamate, and the afterlife, and what pertains to that according to the law of Islam.' And imamate is: general leadership in matters of religion and worldly affairs, as a vicegerency from the Prophet (peace be upon him). By this restriction, prophethood is excluded; by the restriction of generality, such as judgeship and leadership in some regions, as well as the leadership of one whom the imam appoints as his absolute deputy, are excluded, for they are not general imamate.
Imam al-Rāzī said: 'It is general leadership in religion and worldly affairs for a specific person.' He said: 'It is a precaution against [the case of] the entire community when they depose the imam due to his sin.' It seems he meant by 'the entire community' the people of binding and loosing, and he considered their leadership over others or over each individual of the community. Yet it is objected against him that unity (waḥda) is among the conditions of imamate, not among its constitutive elements (muqawwimāt). And among the conditions there are many, and there are proofs for stipulating them. It can be said: It (unity) is more akin to the constitutive elements, because one would not say of the entire community at that time that they are imams, unlike the ignorant or sinful imam, etc. On this basis, one should not say of two persons who have received the community's pledge that they are both imams.
If it is said: 'Vicegerency from the Prophet is only for one whom the Prophet appointed as his successor. So the definition does not apply to the imamate of the pledge (bay'a) and the like, let alone the leadership of the general deputy of the imam.' We say: 'Even if conceded, vicegerency (istikhāf) is more general, whether it be through an intermediary or without one.'
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage explains the inclusion of imamate in the science of kalām and provides definitions. It begins by stating that due to the spread of corrupt beliefs, especially from the Rawāfiḍ (Shīʿa) and Khawārij, which threatened Islamic foundations and slandered the Rightly Guided Caliphs, the mutakallimūn attached the topic of imamate to kalām, even including it in the definition of the science: the science that investigates the principles of the Maker, prophethood, imamate, and the afterlife. Then the author defines imamate itself: general leadership in religion and worldly affairs as a vicegerency (khilāfa) from the Prophet. By 'general,' prophethood is excluded; by 'general,' partial leaderships like judgeship or regional governorship are excluded. Next, he quotes Imam al-Rāzī's definition: general leadership for a specific person, and explains that Rāzī's phrase 'is a precaution against the entire community' refers to the case where the people of binding and loosing depose an imam; he meant that the entire community does not become the imam. An objection is raised that unity (waḥda) is only a condition, not a constitutive element. The author responds that unity is more like a constitutive element because one would not call multiple persons 'imams,' whereas a sinful or ignorant imam is still called imam. Therefore, two persons cannot both be imams even if pledged. Finally, an objection is raised: the definition of imamate as vicegerency from the Prophet only applies to those he directly appointed, not to those chosen by bayʿa. The author answers that vicegerency is general and can be direct or indirect.

Key Terms
إمامة
خلافة
رياسة عامة
روافض
خوارج
وحدة
مقومات
شرائط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that unity (waḥda) is merely a condition (shart) for imamate, not a constitutive element (muqawwim).
Correction: The author argues that unity is more akin to a constitutive element because if multiple persons held imamate, we would not call them 'imams' collectively, whereas an ignorant or sinful imam is still called an imam.

Checkpoint
Why did the mutakallimūn include the topic of imamate in the science of kalām?
A) Because it is a practical ruling like fiqh
B) Because corrupt beliefs from Rawāfiḍ and Khawārij threatened Islamic foundations
C) Because the Prophet commanded it
D) Because it is a branch of theology by necessity

Key Takeaway
Imamate was included in kalām to refute corrupt sectarian beliefs, and its definition as general vicegerency from the Prophet requires careful consideration of conditions like unity, which functions as a constitutive element rather than a mere condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see divisions among Muslims today over leadership and allegiance, do you find yourself leaning toward a fanatical group that slanders other Muslims? What in this passage warns you about the danger of such fanaticism, and how will you actively guard your heart against it starting today?
?
The mutakallimūn included imamate in kalām to protect the foundations of Islam from corrupt beliefs. Is there an area of your own faith where you hold a belief that you have not thoroughly examined? Will you commit to studying it with the same critical care Taftazani applies here?
?
If you were to define the legitimate authority over you in religious and worldly matters, does your definition align with the one given here (general vicegerency from the Prophet)? Who or what currently holds that authority in your life, and are you ready to submit to it fully?

The Obligation of Appointing an Imam: A Survey of Positions
Enumeration of sectarian positions on Imam appointment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various positions held by different Islamic sects on the obligation of appointing an Imam and the basis for that obligation.

Core Idea
Most sects agree on the obligation of an Imam, but differ on its source.

This passage from al-Maqasid outlines the first topic on the appointment of the Imam. It immediately presents a spectrum of views: from the Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila who see it as obligatory by revelation or reason, to the Shi'a who consider it obligatory upon God, to the Kharijites who deny any obligation, and to conditional positions. Understanding this diversity is essential before delving into the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Observe how many distinct positions are mentioned in just a few lines.
Notice the use of 'sam'an' and 'aqlan' – these are key terms.
2
Identify each group's position
List the groups: Ahl al-Sunna, Mu'tazila (general and specific individuals), Shi'a, Najdat, al-Asamm, al-Quti. For each, note whether they say obligatory or not, and on what basis.
Ahl al-Sunna says 'sam'an' (by revelation), some Mu'tazila say 'aqlan', Shi'a says 'upon God', etc.
3
Understand the conditional views
Al-Asamm and al-Quti condition the obligation on circumstances (justice/injustice). This shows that some scholars considered the socio-political context relevant.
4
Consider the footnote on Shi'a
The footnote clarifies the linguistic and political meaning of 'Shi'a'. Reflect on why this clarification might be necessary.
The term 'Shi'a' is used in multiple ways; here it refers to the party supporting the family of Ali.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الأول - نصب الإمام . واجب على الخلق سمعاً عندنا وعند عامة المعتزلة، وعقلاً عند بعضهم، وعلى الله عند الشيعة (١) ، وليس بواجب أصلاً عند النجدات، وحال ظهور العدل عند الأصم ، والظلم عند القوطي. (١) الشيعة المدلول اللغوي للفظ الشيعة هم الأنصار والأتباع ، وأما المدلول السياسي فيقصد به الحزب المناصر لآل البيت بيت علي - رضي الله عنه وكل إمام لا ينسب إلى هذا البيت تعد سلطته غير شرعية عندهم .
First topic - Appointment of the Imam. It is obligatory upon the creation by revelation (sam'an) according to us and according to the general body of the Mu'tazila, and by reason ('aqlan) according to some of them, and obligatory upon God according to the Shi'a (1), and not obligatory at all according to the Najdat, and [obligatory] in the case of the appearance of justice according to al-Asamm, and [obligatory] in the case of injustice according to al-Quti. (1) The Shi'a: the linguistic meaning of the word 'Shi'a' is supporters and followers. As for the political meaning, it denotes the party supporting the family of the Prophet, the family of 'Ali - may God be pleased with him - and any Imam not belonging to this family is considered illegitimate in authority according to them.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage defines the first topic of the discussion: the appointment of the Imam. It immediately states the ruling that it is obligatory, and then enumerates the different positions on the basis of that obligation: whether it is by revelation (sam'an) as held by the Ahl al-Sunna and most Mu'tazila, by reason ('aqlan) for some Mu'tazila, or obligatory upon God for the Shi'a. It also notes that the Najdat (a Kharijite subsect) deny obligation entirely, while al-Asamm and al-Quti (both Mu'tazila) condition it on circumstances of justice or injustice. The footnote clarifies the term 'Shi'a'.

Key Terms
نصب الإمام
سمعاً
عقلاً
النجدات
الأصم
القوطي
الشيعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the obligation is purely rational across all groups.
Correction: The passage shows that the majority (Ahl al-Sunna and general Mu'tazila) hold it as obligatory by revelation, not reason. Only some Mu'tazila base it on reason.

Checkpoint
According to the Ahl al-Sunna, how is the appointment of the Imam obligatory?
A) By reason ('aqlan)
B) By revelation (sam'an)
C) It is not obligatory at all
D) Upon God

Key Takeaway
The appointment of an Imam is generally considered obligatory, but the basis for this obligation varies across Islamic sects—from revelation and reason to divine obligation and conditional circumstances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the different positions on the obligation of an Imam, which one resonates most with your own understanding of authority? What does that say about your view of God's role in establishing leadership?
?
The Najdat rejected any obligation for an Imam. In what areas of your life do you resist authority or structure? Is that resistance based on principle or convenience? How might that affect your spiritual accountability?
?
The Shi'a believe it is obligatory upon God to appoint an Imam. How does your concept of God's justice—whether you believe God must do certain things or is free from compulsion—shape your acceptance or rejection of this view? Are you willing to submit to God's decree even if it challenges your reasoning?

What Is Kalam?
intermediate
5 min
Al-Ghazali on the Hidden Nature of Specific Merit
Al-Ghazali explains the hidden nature of merit and lists specific individuals and groups known from texts to be among the people of Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ghazali's view that true merit is known only to God and the Prophet, and that specific individuals have been affirmed in revelation.

Core Idea
True merit is hidden but affirmed for those God has chosen.

Al-Ghazali begins by distinguishing between the ultimate reality of merit, known only to Allah and His Messenger, and the specific individuals whose virtue has been attested to in revealed texts. This passage sets the stage for understanding that while the precise ranking is obscure, certain companions and family members are assured of Paradise.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ghazali's opening statement
Read the first part of the passage where al-Ghazali states that the reality of merit is with God and known only to the Prophet.
Notice his emphasis on the hiddenness of the full ranking.
2
Identify the list of individuals
Find the names and groups mentioned: Fatima, Hasan, Husayn, people of Bay'at al-Ridwan, participants of Badr, Uhud, and Hudaybiyya, and the ten Companions.
3
Reflect on the significance of the list
Consider why al-Ghazali says only those who witnessed revelation understand the ranking, yet he still provides a specific list from texts.
This shows that while the full ranking is hidden, textual indications are clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام الغزالي ( رحمة الله تعالى عليه : حقيقة الفضل ما هو عند الله ، وذلك مما لا يطلع عليه إلا رسول الله . وقد ورد في الثناء عليهم أخبار كثيرة، ولا يدرك دقائق الفضل والترتيب فيه إلا المشاهدون للوحي والتنزيل بقرائن الأحوال. فلولا فهم ذلك، لما رتبوا الأمر كذلك إذ كان لا تأخذهم في الله لومة لائم، ولا يصرفهم عن الحق صارف، وأما فيمن عداهم فقد ورد النص بأن فاطمة سيدة نساء أهل الجنة ، وأن الحسن والحسين سيدا شباب أهل الجنة ، وأن أهل بيعة الرضوان الذين بايعوه تحت الشجرة ، ومن شهد بدراً وأحداً والحديبية من أهل الجنة، وحديث بشارة العشرة بالجنة مشهور يكاد يلحق بالمتواترات وهم : أبو بكر، وعمر، وعثمان ، وعلي ، وطلحة والزبير، وعبد الرحمن بن عوف، وسعد بن أبي وقاص، وسعيد بن زيد، وأبو عبيدة بن الجراح . وأما إجمالاً فقد تطابق الكتاب والسنة، والإجماع على أن الفضل للعلم والتقوى . قال الله تعالى : ( إن أكرمكم عند الله أتقاكم (٢) . وقال الله تعالى : قل هل يستوي الذين يعلمون والذين لا يعلمون ) (۳) . وقال الله تعالى : يرفع الله الذين آمنوا منكم والذين أوتوا العلم درجات ) (٤) . وقال النبي ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) : « الناس سواسية كأسنان المشط ، لا فضل لعربي على عجمي، إنما الفضل بالتقوى ) . وقال عليه السلام) : إن فضل العالم على العابد كفضل القمر ليلة البدر على سائر الكواكب .» . وإن العلماء ورثة الأنبياء .
Imam al-Ghazali (may God have mercy on him) said: The reality of merit is what is with God, and that is something that none can know except the Messenger of God. Many reports have come in praise of them, and the subtleties of merit and its ranking are only grasped by those who witnessed the revelation and the sending down through contextual clues. Had they not understood that, they would not have arranged matters so, since they were not deterred by any reproach in God, nor did any hinderer turn them from the truth. And as for those besides them, the text has come that Fatima is the mistress of the women of Paradise, and that al-Hasan and al-Husayn are the masters of the youth of Paradise, and that the people of the Pledge of Ridwan who pledged allegiance under the tree, and those who witnessed Badr, Uhud, and Hudaybiyya are from the people of Paradise. And the hadith of the glad tidings of the ten to Paradise is well-known, nearly reaching the level of mutawatir. They are: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Sa'id ibn Zayd, and Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah. And in general, the Book, the Sunna, and the consensus agree that virtue is for knowledge and piety. God Almighty said: 'Indeed, the most honorable of you with God is the most righteous among you' (49:13). And God Almighty said: 'Say, are those who know equal to those who do not know?' (39:9). And God Almighty said: 'God will raise those who have believed among you and those who have been given knowledge, by degrees' (58:11). And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'People are as equal as the teeth of a comb; no superiority of an Arab over a non-Arab except by piety.' And he (peace be upon him) said: 'The superiority of a scholar over a worshiper is like the superiority of the full moon over all other stars.' And indeed the scholars are the inheritors of the prophets.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage contains a quote from Imam al-Ghazali followed by scriptural proofs. Al-Ghazali begins by stating that true merit (al-fadl) is known only to God, and only the Messenger of God can know it. Many praises have come, but the precise ranking of merit is only understood by those who were present at revelation. He then lists specific individuals who are known from texts to be among the people of Paradise: Fatima, Hasan, Husayn, the people of Bay'at al-Ridwan, participants of Badr, Uhud, and Hudaybiyya, and the ten companions (the 'ashara mubashshara). He notes that the hadith of the ten is widely known. After al-Ghazali's quote, the author adds that in general (ijmālan), the Quran, Sunna, and consensus agree that virtue is for knowledge and piety. He then cites three Quranic verses: Surah al-Hujurat (49:13) emphasizing taqwa, Surah al-Zumar (39:9) contrasting knowledge with ignorance, and Surah al-Mujadala (58:11) on raising those with knowledge. He also cites two hadiths: one on equality of people by taqwa, and another on the superiority of the scholar over the worshiper, concluding that scholars are inheritors of prophets.

Key Terms
حقيقة الفضل
رسول الله
فاطمة
الحسن والحسين
أهل بيعة الرضوان
العشرة المبشرون بالجنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ghazali denies that any specific merit can be known or assigned to individuals.
Correction: Al-Ghazali actually affirms that texts have come praising specific individuals and groups, showing their merit is known through revelation even if the full ranking is with God.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who can know the true reality of merit?
A) All believers
B) Only the Messenger of God
C) The scholars
D) The prophets

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali teaches that while the exact ranking of merit is known only to God, revelation has singled out certain individuals as being among the people of Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ghazali says the reality of merit is hidden with God. Do you secretly compare your own spiritual status to others, measuring yourself by your deeds or reputation? Will you today entrust that judgment entirely to Allah and instead focus solely on what He has commanded you?
?
The Prophet knew the merit of those around him. Do you truly submit to the Prophet's guidance as sufficient for your salvation, or do you rely on your own reasoning and self-assessment? What step can you take this week to increase your reliance on revelation over personal opinion?
?
The Companions and the Prophet's family are explicitly mentioned as people of Paradise. Does your love for them move you to emulate their sacrifices and loyalty, or is it limited to verbal admiration? What specific action will you take today to follow their example in obedience to Allah?

What Is Kalam?
