Scriptural Proofs: Virtue by Knowledge and Piety
Cites Quranic verses and hadiths to prove that virtue is based on knowledge and piety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn the Quranic and hadith proofs that virtue is based on knowledge and piety, not on lineage or status.

Core Idea
True virtue is measured by knowledge and piety, not by worldly attributes.

After discussing specific individuals, the author turns to the general consensus that virtue is for knowledge and piety. This section presents three Quranic verses and two hadiths that establish this principle clearly.

Guided Path
1
Read the general claim
Read the opening sentence that the Book, Sunna, and consensus agree that virtue is for knowledge and piety.
2
Examine the Quranic verses
Identify each verse and note its main message: 49:13 (taqwa), 39:9 (knowledge vs ignorance), 58:11 (raising those with knowledge).
3
Examine the hadiths
Read the hadiths: one on equality, one on scholar's superiority, and one on scholars as inheritors. Understand how they reinforce the principle.
4
Synthesize the principle
Combine all proofs to conclude that virtue is based on knowledge and piety alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام الغزالي ( رحمة الله تعالى عليه : حقيقة الفضل ما هو عند الله ، وذلك مما لا يطلع عليه إلا رسول الله . وقد ورد في الثناء عليهم أخبار كثيرة، ولا يدرك دقائق الفضل والترتيب فيه إلا المشاهدون للوحي والتنزيل بقرائن الأحوال. فلولا فهم ذلك، لما رتبوا الأمر كذلك إذ كان لا تأخذهم في الله لومة لائم، ولا يصرفهم عن الحق صارف، وأما فيمن عداهم فقد ورد النص بأن فاطمة سيدة نساء أهل الجنة ، وأن الحسن والحسين سيدا شباب أهل الجنة ، وأن أهل بيعة الرضوان الذين بايعوه تحت الشجرة ، ومن شهد بدراً وأحداً والحديبية من أهل الجنة، وحديث بشارة العشرة بالجنة مشهور يكاد يلحق بالمتواترات وهم : أبو بكر، وعمر، وعثمان ، وعلي ، وطلحة والزبير، وعبد الرحمن بن عوف، وسعد بن أبي وقاص، وسعيد بن زيد، وأبو عبيدة بن الجراح . وأما إجمالاً فقد تطابق الكتاب والسنة، والإجماع على أن الفضل للعلم والتقوى . قال الله تعالى : ( إن أكرمكم عند الله أتقاكم (٢) . وقال الله تعالى : قل هل يستوي الذين يعلمون والذين لا يعلمون ) (۳) . وقال الله تعالى : يرفع الله الذين آمنوا منكم والذين أوتوا العلم درجات ) (٤) . وقال النبي ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) : « الناس سواسية كأسنان المشط ، لا فضل لعربي على عجمي، إنما الفضل بالتقوى ) . وقال عليه السلام) : إن فضل العالم على العابد كفضل القمر ليلة البدر على سائر الكواكب .» . وإن العلماء ورثة الأنبياء .
Imam al-Ghazali (may God have mercy on him) said: The reality of merit is what is with God, and that is something that none can know except the Messenger of God. Many reports have come in praise of them, and the subtleties of merit and its ranking are only grasped by those who witnessed the revelation and the sending down through contextual clues. Had they not understood that, they would not have arranged matters so, since they were not deterred by any reproach in God, nor did any hinderer turn them from the truth. And as for those besides them, the text has come that Fatima is the mistress of the women of Paradise, and that al-Hasan and al-Husayn are the masters of the youth of Paradise, and that the people of the Pledge of Ridwan who pledged allegiance under the tree, and those who witnessed Badr, Uhud, and Hudaybiyya are from the people of Paradise. And the hadith of the glad tidings of the ten to Paradise is well-known, nearly reaching the level of mutawatir. They are: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Sa'id ibn Zayd, and Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah. And in general, the Book, the Sunna, and the consensus agree that virtue is for knowledge and piety. God Almighty said: 'Indeed, the most honorable of you with God is the most righteous among you' (49:13). And God Almighty said: 'Say, are those who know equal to those who do not know?' (39:9). And God Almighty said: 'God will raise those who have believed among you and those who have been given knowledge, by degrees' (58:11). Commentary
This passage contains a quote from Imam al-Ghazali followed by scriptural proofs. Al-Ghazali begins by stating that true merit (al-fadl) is known only to God, and only the Messenger of God can know it. Many praises have come, but the precise ranking of merit is only understood by those who were present at revelation. Key Terms
الفضل للعلم والتقوى
الناس سواسية كأسنان المشط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that tribal lineage or ethnicity determines religious merit.
Correction: The Quran and hadith explicitly state that virtue is by piety and knowledge, and that all people are equal in basic humanity.

Checkpoint
Which verse is cited to show that those who know are not equal to those who do not know?
A) 49:13
B) 39:9
C) 58:11
D) 2:269

Key Takeaway
The Islamic scripture and consensus establish that virtue is based solely on knowledge and piety, not on lineage or worldly status.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If virtue is truly only by knowledge and piety, what does that mean for the ways you seek validation from others? Are you more concerned with how you appear or with what you know and how you fear Allah?
?
The hadith says scholars are like the full moon among stars. Are you striving to be among those scholars, or are you content with being a distant star? What is one concrete step you will take this week to gain beneficial knowledge?
?
You have just read that no Arab has superiority over a non-Arab except by piety. Is there a person you look down upon because of their ethnicity, tribe, or social status? How will you actively change your heart to honor them solely for their taqwa?
